Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 One method is that you make three or four cauterizations, following the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cautery we have said before; and do not rush your hand over the entire cautery, and let the patient be aware on his back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and clear the cavity that is near the mouse, or the incisions made by the patient come from the left side, and lift the elevations from the cavity according to the body, and the cauterizations should be according to the size of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After that, put the two inflamed nerves in such a way that the incisions are pierced from the other side, and then pull out the fire-cautery; so there will be four openings. And if you see, cauterize the entire cautery at three openings.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After it has poured pus for a long time, and this is good that the other of the said treatments be applied next.
de ydropisie	dropisy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 Cauterizing does not help for dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When your treatment according to the methods we have mentioned in divisions does not help, then you must make four cauterizations around the abdomen, and one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back near the spine, and one at the worst place; and let the cauteries be close to the thick part of the incision.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the fire cautery open for a long time to expel pus, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the clavicle as we have shown before; and for the back it should be olive oil, as it has been previously stated.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the inflammation of feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 When the feet are swollen in a person suffering from dropsy and filled with yellow liquid, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and dip your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not go too deep, otherwise the yellow liquid will flow out forcefully; and let the cautery be of this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making .2 cauteries for each leg with the tip of the knife; let one cautery be long, located in front of the knee and the other behind it, within the leg; leave the cauteries above for a long time to cure, allowing the citric acid to settle; after healing the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	treatment of edema
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the swelling of the abdomen comes from cold and moisture, while the digestive and retentive virtues that are in the stomach and intestines are blocked, and cannot be cured by means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong constitution, then do one large cautery on the stomach as mentioned before (cautery of the stomach), around the circle; and four subtle cauteries around the navel, one subtle cautery clavile, and two cauteries on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, do a cautery on the joint, and one cautery on each isle, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure for hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 When hemorrhoids are deep-rooted or there are more than one, and they are old, thick with cold, corrupted humors, cured as we have said in the divisions, and it does not help if you do cauteries: III on the spine of the back, that which is entirely turned outwards under the ribs, moving triangularly, and the cautery below the navel; if you think that his stomach is cooled and the flesh is not cooking, and you see the face swelling, then the face receives a large cautery on the stomach as stated before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with the whole cautery pointed; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the shoulder when it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the charnoisiteit which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you burn the ulcer, heat the cautery that seems like a razor, and then put it all over the ulcer being burned; and let your hand be there until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, thus burning it clean; do this once or twice, and if there is much ulcer, cauterize each one as we have said; after the care of ointments useful until they are healed; and if you cauterize a large cautery on the bladder, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	From an improperly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will describe in its place, this disease comes that can only be healed by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 If any abscess comes, and it is filled with pus and corrupt moisture, you must test the entire tent (or cavity) with extreme caution, and ensure that you understand the entire extent of the corruption.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 After heating the cautery that resembles a razor, insert it into the abscess according to the size of the cavity, and repeat the cauterization until the body and corruption are burned once or twice, depending on the amount of pus required; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are near, and the main veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 If the abscess goes to the body of the bladder or intestines, beware of these areas, and do not perform this procedure outside a charnut (a type of wood), and think that it is not perforated; after curing the shoulder when it is healthy, if the shoulders are septic, and the matter has been removed for a long time, understand that the shoulder is completely healed; if the matter is not removed, understand that the shoulder is fractured, and the bone is corrupted in this way, as one of those we will describe in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of cold comes to the kidneys and of large swelling, and it does not take on female form, then it is necessary that you perform cautery over the kidneys from both sides with the clavicle cautery as we have previously said; and if we cauterize in milk, it will have four cauteries in line, and it will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft due to cold or moisture, and the patient retains urine, then make a fire cautery in the area outside the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right side and one on the left side, and both should be as long as the little finger; and make one incision behind the back, or two if needed; and the incisions should be parallel to each other according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	of the kidney
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the kidney is cold and moist and cannot conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their term is delayed; and when they come, it causes great pain: then you must make four cauteries around the belly, as we have said in the caution of the bladder, and two cauteries behind the back; and the incisions should be parallel to each other, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the wound
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors sink into the wound of the thigh, and for this reason it becomes silent from its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joints of the limb are found to be separated, if you must cauterize the patient on the wound of the thigh with .i. cautery resembling a circle, and sign in front of the joint around the wound so that the wound is within the circle; and if the cauteries are like those with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make four large olive-shaped cauteries, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the haunch
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hollow of the haunch, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated as we have said in the division but the cure is of no use, and the illness is old: therefore you must purge the patient from the large humors with fetid pills or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 After that, perform the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two ways: namely with burning substances, and cautery with fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 The other way of the fire cautery is as follows: you should cauterize on the boil of the haunch with three triangular cauteries according to this shape, and make it deep and large, and have space between each cautionary of the size of a thumb, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes one cauterizes in the middle on the chief of the haunch, for which there are four according to this shape.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, cauterize the circular cautery in the dislocation of the shoulder blade; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire shoulder blade, and all the edges of the wound are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain remains in the haunch and does not reach either the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if it comes up to the thigh and leg, make II fire cauteries where the patient says the pain is, and the fire cautery 4 fingers above the ankle, on the left side a little; and let the cautery be a surgical tool, and let the shaft of the coal be dry; and if the patient feels that the pain spreads to the toes or near there, cauterize where he feels the pain 3 times or 4 using the cautery called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, do more; and if the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, apply a cautery with a cutlery or circular tool, but be careful in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery too much so as to burn nerves and large arteries, and not to cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 I myself have seen more who made a cautery above the ankle on the foot and allowed it to remain until the leg swelled completely and the toes also, and they were pierced and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a stomach solution, he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 If the pain is in two parts together, perform cautery on one and the other, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And in the cautery of the haunch, they will say as follows for this method, make such iron and be as thick as a nail of the thumb or slightly less, and be between the bones or from one bone to another at a distance equal to the size of a nut from the knuckle; and the spaces between the bones should be above two parts, and they should be like nuts, and it should have a well-made iron handle; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it up until it becomes completely red and boiling hot, and then put it on the ill ankle, turning it towards the healthy side; and cauterize once with a single cautery and let it rest for four days. Then apply plaster made of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this fire cautery due to its fearsome aspect, and few know how to use it effectively; however, it is one of the good cauteries, which can be endured by those who can, and where it can be applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The cautery of medicine burns such that you make the instrument between the bones in which pierces the margin of the door, and it should be made of iron or steel one part long, and at the top have two nuts, and between each have the size of a pea; and they should be turned outward and upward, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 After placing the hot iron on the patient's shoulder lying on a soft surface, place your hand very close to the hot iron on the patient's shoulder; afterwards pour the boiling water between the two circles of the hot iron which has been heated over the fire for a while, and leave it for an hour, enduring the heat and burning for the patient.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it burns similarly as fire; and when the burning has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the shoulder gently with soft water, and leave it for three days; apply butter until the blackness from the burn is removed; and let it be for three more days until it has healed; this would be the final aid after the cure of ointments until it becomes healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And if the pain has spread to the thigh or the leg, make him lie down on his back as you have done in the previous case; and this is the method of hot oil, which I have written or treated regarding the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take quicklime and hot coals, equal amounts of each, grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 Or have it placed with a small hole covered so that the tip of a razor can enter; and put this pot on another well-sealed pot, and put hot oil, soft oil, on top until you have reached the desired thickness with your hand; and leave it like that until the powder descends into the pot or the pot is well sealed, then take all that oil and pour it over hot coals and lime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then if it [the dislocated limb] becomes very hot and is administered for the works of medicine and cauterizing other members, as it does similar work like fire, and if there are other medicines with which the hankle is cauterized well, such as wax, honey, anise seed, almond oil, and soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 Galen tells us of a cure by which a nobleman was cured of the pain in his leg and sciatica, and he praised it highly, saying that no other cure was made for it, and that it was cured once when this cure was made, and he was bathed as he instructs below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says that you should take dried green vervain, grind it finely with a little fat, place it on the affected leg and thigh and on the part where the pain is felt, and hold it in place; leave it for three hours, so that the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then make him enter the bath until his body is slightly warmed up, and let him lie in it, and the pain will leave completely and he will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 Know that no one should use such fire cautery medicine unless after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's fat, it helps much; and the cautery should be made in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take linen and beat it with old oil, and put it on the depression that is between the toe of the foot and the one called the foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 Then take dry goat's fat, heat it on fire until it becomes charcoal, and put it on the linen, and let it stay there; repeat this again and do not stop until you think with your senses that it reaches the hunch, and the pain is stopped; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat's fat".
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether it be from falling or impact or too much evacuation, or like the effects of cold matter spreading, none of these symptoms call for cauteries, except in the case of cold matter infusion.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after this, that the patient be emptied of foul pills or similar things, which are to be placed on the back, where the pain is felt, three lines marked with ink, and in each line 5 or more cauteries according to the strength and quantity that the patient can tolerate; and the cautery should be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, do 4 cauteries or 2 according to the medium-sized cautery in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Often this disease comes to small children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a narrow anus when they become constipated, and fear; and you find in the lower spine on the back and in our appearance which appears above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this shape.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 The cautery increases each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you see, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointed at intervals of 2 or 3 lines and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 After healing the joint when it is healed according to what we have said, ensure that you do not apply caution in a sciatica state that is in the nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	"of the pain of the joints"
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	"When the pain of the joints is due to moisture that has spread throughout all members of the body and when the pain occurs in the feet, which are called "podagre" properly, and when it is from cold causes and medicines cannot cure it, it is treated with cauteries as follows: make a hot iron cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:"
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary to prick on the thigh, let it be cauterized all over with the cautery called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pain comes to the genitals and other joints, which often happens, let it be cauterized on each knee with 3 or 4 cauteries in each part, all over with the olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do more, but keep your hand away except that the core of the coal is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend to the genitals and back, administer the fire cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are in the hands, make a puncture twice fingers' length around the wrist; and if no pain remains in the thumb, make a puncture above each joint and above the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and administer medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you take good care of him and purge the fever, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the nose
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When eruptions come in anger, and the bowels descend to the kidneys and this is new, it is necessary that when you wish to cure it, you must not let him eat that day; and he should use things which relax the stomach, so that the feces descend from his stomach; afterwards have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his flank as long as the bowels are repaired, and hold them at your sides, and sign with a mark like half of a circle above the abdomen; then heat the cautery in the shape as shown here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 as long as it is white and it exudes pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then fix the dislocated joints in their place; and the attendant holds his hand above so that it does not return to its previous position; and work well on the patient's thighs, put a cushion and a sergeant on his thighs, and another one on the affected side which holds the hands; then put the cautery on the affected area with your entire hand, hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you reach the bone; be careful that the dislocated joint does not move when you perform the cautery; avoid burning it; and thus the patient will not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And the cauteries for children should be subtle according to their size, and for large people as big as they are; after three days heal the level of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; after that, heal it with other unguents until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound heals well; and it is necessary to let his urine be stopped for a long time, so that the bowels do not protrude when he wants to go to the chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after forty days, when he wants to get up, bring a broad bandage and keep it for another forty days; let him have good rest, so that he does not overwork himself or eat too much and drink too much, nor talk too loudly; and when he follows this instruction, he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I shall tell you next about the treatment of amputation in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the wound from the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When round worms appear in other bellies and are recognized as not growing anymore, if you do the fire cautery according to its quantity, it should burn the third part of the stomach; after the cure according to what has been said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the place of entry and make a line above the worm, and another below, and then press your hand on the whole three-angled cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cauteries are lighter and more movable.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes in any limb, either from falling or being hurt, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medicine cures do not help, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, and its virtue and location for twisting and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If the first cautery is discharged, it's good; if not, start another cautery on the same, because this custom is that it should heal in the limb that is nearby, so you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	To mix (or compound) medicine
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 These illnesses are sometimes helped by cautery with great effort, and especially the diseases that come from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 Can you see the patient being cauterized, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, neither dissolve nor stay, and you doubt that the corruption may affect the entire patient, then perform V cauteries on the head: hold the head downwards, and the other towards the front to the end of the hairs; and II at the II horns, and I behind the haiterel; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and so that the scabs come out forcefully so that the vapors of the gross humors may escape; and cauterize over the mice according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the medicine has spread all over, it will surely disappear, then you must cauterize with those cauteries we have mentioned on the head, and one cautery at the nape of the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one at the buttock and another under it, and two on each shoulder; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the legs, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and over the hollows of the hands; be careful not to burn the nerves that are above the lower back, and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more you perform the fire cautery, the more aid you give, and it benefits them; and know that patients do not feel pain during the cautery as the healthy ones do, because their bodies are already all corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 The cautionery should be deep and shallow according to the members and joints, as you will find in ways of using irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After curing the shoulder with flour and honey, and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If a swelling appears in any member and is treated with medicine, oils, plasters and it is not healed, then make cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness of the member; and let the cauterization be a little deep into the flesh; then cure it with liniments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes they make a fire cautery on the hand, foot, and back, at the end of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and in this way if it is cut off the flesh; but no one should interfere with it unless he knows the members and the ends of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	From the linen cloth [or fabric]
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is recognized, and the instruments of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a shallow cautery, according to the thickness of the skin involved, until the blister is removed and the color changes; then cure it with flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, as well as pig's blood and goose blood, each in equal parts; mix everything together and bind it with a cloth; apply it to the location until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	treating canker with cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When the boil starts and you see it begin to spread, if you want to stop it, you should cauterize with a fire cautery that resembles a circle around the boil.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 But the wise say that a fire cautery should be made in the middle of the boil; but this does not seem good to me, because it causes the ulcer to become corrupt, and I have seen it happen sometimes; instead, it should be cauterized around, with the fire cautery called "circular," as we have said in our discussion on cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot grow
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has a disease called "adubelati", which is slow to heal due to its excess or the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, very old) and has little blood, or for some other reason it appears to be hastened in healing; then you shall cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking: afterwards leave it as it is.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 It will heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced entirely with the fire cautery, heat the cautery as shown here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 Place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the core, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them outside in such a way that the course of the pus is made more evident.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the cure until it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another kind of disease is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than the consumption of a limb, as it corrodes them as fire dries up wet things.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this disease in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cauterizing irons both small and large, according to what is needed in the place or the location of the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you have reached all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, remove everything that has been corrupted.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and apply soft soothing cauterized with oil on the wounds from fire and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the cure of onions producing charcoal.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if you see after three days that healthy char does not grow, it is good; and if not, repeat the cautery on the corrupted lesion.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 This application is sometimes cured with medicine for fever instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure for fever in the division: take it when needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The coming pricks to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 Very often a disease called "closed" (according to our understanding) arises from the feet, which is a large thing swollen that presses on the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries of this disease are according to two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 This is to know fire cautery and water hot cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 This means: The fire cautery is when you heat the cautery as thin as a feather from a goose quill, made of good iron that can pierce through the nail in all directions and has fine edges; after that, put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it reaches the point of the nail; leave it like this for three days until it starts to show signs of pus formation; then apply a plaster made of malicious herbs boiled with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will shrink and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the shoulder with soothing salve until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if it has been turned outwards by falling from the body, and it often happens in hands and feet, you must apply hot cautery; and this is done as follows: take a wire of iron or copper, or a pen from the plow, and place it on the nail and the sore; that is, to pierce warts; and place the wire around so that it surrounds entirely, then put a little hot coal there and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the margin of the wire comes to the root of the nail, and may find the hot coal penetrating deeply up to the root; and let the patient endure a little biting of the hot coal for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will remove itself with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 Thus, do after another, as long as you heat all those who are in the body, then cure them with ointments that soften flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The Cure for Shaking (or Trembling)
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	For anyone who shakes due to coldness of the nerves, or quartan fever or another, you should apply four or five cauteries on the spinal column between each spine; one cautery in the buttocks and one on the stomach using an olive oil cautery; this will stop the shaking and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of putrid pustules (or boils)
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes on the outside of the body appear baths, or pustules rotten, which come from large corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 At first when they appear, it is necessary to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery from myrtle stick, so that the tip is seized by fire, or from a long root of aristolochia, or to a cautery lenticular.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes cauterize on the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow from behind, but the superfluous parts from which they come are destroyed, and they heal; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great evacuations of blood from the cut artery in the wound that appears on the surface or at the incision of an abscess or the cauterization of a member, and similar things; it is a very serious matter to bleed out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	However, when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound vein and hold it very tight until the blood is stopped flowing; then apply the olive oil cauterizer (smaller or larger) as many times as necessary until it is all red; next take .i., either large or small depending on the size of the wound and the location in which the artery is severed, and place the cauterizer on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cauterizer there until the bleeding has been stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a jump occurs when you place your hand on the vein, and the fire cautery is extinguished, take immediately another cautery that is near the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	Continue to do this one after the other until the vein is closed; and beware not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and let no further harm come upon the patient; know that when blood stops flowing from the artery, it cannot be properly stopped when the artery is large unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated beforehand, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed on it that can stop the blood; and let it be tied and constricted accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the constriction of a narrow ligature or placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit if it does not help.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone who has neither sight nor medicine at hand, he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out until it remains swollen above the wound and the vein; and he must not move it, but the cold moisture should often be applied so that it becomes very cold until the wound is frozen and thickened and remains swollen; and make inquiries in advance for the cauteries and medicines needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgeries (or heals)
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and we explained the origins and instruments and forms of cauteries; I placed that chapter on the head to the feet, and I will proceed with this chapter in the same way because those things are easier to understand when they are presented in order.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of this, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I warn you to not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many ways of men come in treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 There come also those who are so afflicted by their disease that they die quickly due to the ferocity of their illness and the severity of their malady; and these should be feared.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And among these there is one who gives his sense and says: "wait, I am cured"; and the illness is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 You must not easily consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more confidence in your honor than in your desire, and do not reveal lightly but wisely from those of whom you are certain, and from which you have experience; and use prediction and indication in treating your patients so that salvation is attained; and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, come.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Moreover, I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into sections, according to that which is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have explained from head to feet, because you will find it easier to understand those matters from which you will need assistance.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often comes to children during birth, and when the head of the child is pressed too hard; and sometimes it happens due to a reason that we are not aware of.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone but children, and for all those I have seen, death was swift; therefore, it seems to me that it is worthwhile to stop the work in some treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and it swelled each day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture collected under the skull between the brain and the bone; and the treatments are such that if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a large incision in the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture flows out; and here is the form of the lancet:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see the fissures of the head are opened on each side, and they do not respond when you press them from within, then it is necessary that you make four cuts in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 Then straighten the incisions with linen cloths and powders, and put wine and oil on it, leave it like that until the fifth day; then undress it, and heal the wound with bandages and ointments, and keep the head swollen, and give the patient dry meat without moisture as much as the member is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incising is that you examine the size of the abscess, and gather the pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then make the incision according to what you can, and be careful not to cut the artery; and let some blood flow out, so that the patient dies a proper death due to blood loss and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of remedy
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone with a disease called "catarrah" in the eyes or at its worst, and the disease is old, and medicine does not help, then the last cure is the cautery on the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Therefore, when you want to cover them, the patient should be behind his head; afterwards he rubs the place with a rough cloth on the neck until the arteries appear, then hold the patient's neck with a piece of cloth; then look where the veins are biting, and the left and right are after the ears, and the points are opposite each other; then mark the places with a sharp spatula of two parts, cutting as far as the bone, and this should be through the wide part of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it (the artery), push the sharp spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting as you would through two.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it jumps up without ceasing continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And if the artery does not open on its own, you should measure the space of three fingers width, then press and pierce up to the bone; and it is necessary to put six cubits of blood outside, and perhaps a little more or less according to what the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if it remains above the bone point without swelling, if the pus that comes out from the abscess does not appear, then hold the wound closed and bind it until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of emigration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old emigration comes and acute catarrh arrives, due to the moisture of tears and the heat in the temples, and an old foolish person becomes senile with similar things; it is treated by methods of medicine, but it does not help at all. If the arteries in the temples are opened and cauterized, as we have mentioned, it will help.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient pulls back the hairs at the base of his temples, and listens to the opening artery in the temple because it opens well through beating. It can be easily found except in some cold men. If it is found, the patient strains its neck with some cloth, then rubs the place with a rough cloth and moistens the place with hot water until the arteries appear clearly; then take the spatula of this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up to the prongs and carefully separate all the tissues that are underneath from each side; if the artery is thin, turn it to the tip of the scalpel, then cut off that part according to the size of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 If it is not cut (or punctured), it will not heal at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the .vj. c/, up to .iij.; and if the arteries are large, it is necessary that you tie it with a double strong silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound is closed and bleeding stops; then cut off the excess between the two ligatures at that same hour, and if you see fit, cauterize the wound with the cautery knife up to the bone until the pieces are cut through; and this is the moveable work, if the patient does not have fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauteries are aid for finishing the injuries: which is of greater help to the injured.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary that one fill the area with old cotton and put a well-made tourniquet on top; and when you loosen them, cure it with dry medicines that cause charring, and with tourniquets, until it is healed; and if without the incision of the artery as much as you work, you hurry to cover it by cautery, or use vitriol and squeeze your hand so that the wound does not bleed; and if this is not present, put your hand on the area until it freezes, and rub the area with cold water until it stops bleeding, and squeeze as necessary; and the moveable and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this sharp cautery knife, but the cuts should be well spaced to keep the heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the thermometer is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should be between two knuckles, one of which is thicker in space, and when you have inserted it into the vein by two leagues, and you heat the iron hot until it reaches the bone, and then cut the vein in two leagues; and they should be spaced between two joints because it is not always welded with this cautery all over; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes run down the veins that are above the head of the face and medicine treatment does not help it, and you see the patient frowning, and notice his forehead trembling like shivers; and if they are tender and moist so that the eyelashes fall out, and the eyelids are scalded by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 They called the ancient remedy for this disease "contused cure", and you should shave the patient's hair, both at the front, then make three equal incisions in the forehead along the length of the forehead; one of the incisions should be like this, namely from one end of the forehead to the other, below the eyebrows, and the others two should be at the sides above the eyebrows, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are at the sides above the eyebrows; also keep your hand away from the continuation of the jaws, and let each wound be the size of three fingers joined together; and prepare a piece of sponge and a lot of linen for wiping the blood, then insert the sharp spatula two parts deep as shown here:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.
