The first incision is made from the temple down to the second incision; and peel off all the cartilage that is between the two cuts on top of the bone, then proceed from the middle incision down to the other second, and pull out this spatula-like instrument.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert the instrument called "cultellaire" in the first incision; it is well sharpened on one side, and on the other side it is soft, not sharp, and it has this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And cut the bone towards the flesh at the chosen spot, and the bone becomes soft towards the bone, and push it until it comes to the mid-split.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And completely cut the veins that descend from the head of the eyes until the incision is continuous to where it opens up at the chosen spot, and then continue into the mid-split to the other opening; and then equalize the blood and press the place for the blood taken; then put in each split a tent made of old cotton, and put on top damp cloths soaked in wine, oil, and vinegar, and make sure no pus comes out; and on the third day, undo the suture, and apply a large amount of cold poultice of mustard seed, then treat it with ointment of basilicon with oil of roses, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a sharp catarrh usually comes, and you see the hairs becoming thin and small, and the vision becomes dimmed, and paper burnt; and the hair falls out, and the head aches with acute pain, and the patient coughs; then know by these symptoms that those materials and this catarrh do not come from just one vein, but several. And the cure that is to be made if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And you command the patient to bend his head back, then make a deep cut along the forehead and another wide one at the temples.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 Begin the cut from the left temple to the right temple, and make it to the bone; move your hand away from the nerves that move when eating; when the bone is exposed, squeeze all the blood onto a sponge, then press between the two edges of the cut and put old cotton in, and bind with linen; then cover with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be careful not to create an abscess; when it is removed, you should massage the bone until char tissue begins to grow, then treat with things that encourage char growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour, and 4 parts of colophony, and make a plaster with them; administer it in these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the earstopping
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, animals, stones or similar things like iron; seeds, such as peas, beans or lentils; or flowing things such as water and silks and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear, stone or otherwise, if it does not fit in the ear or does not grow within the ear, place the ear on the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see a stone, distill some purple oil or camphor oil, then apply extraction; and have the person cough with constriction, and stop up the nostrils when coughing comes, and place pieces of fabric or wool around the ear; and stretch it out above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Often comes farting with this cure; and if it does not come farting, apply extraction by fine tweezers, in which case the following is the procedure:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with tweezers, that is good; if not, apply extraction with fine and slender onion or a needle, and if it does not come out by this means, make a cane from beeswax and push the head of the cane or ear tube deeply into the ear so that nothing can enter with the cane; then pull it out forcefully, as often times pus comes in this way; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take glue of whatever kind you have on hand, and place it around an instrument suitable for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatnot, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump out with all these things we have said, you should hurry to incise the ear before an abscess comes, and spasm occurs; and the method of incision is that you first cleanse the patient's head and draw blood according to the measure of its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fat or the place it depends on; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it immediately into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is swollen and growing, administer extraction; and if it cannot be drained, administer a thin and fine probe according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist due to ear moisture, as long as you have made many incisions; then extract it with subtle forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Therefore in case of water that falls into the ear, the patient should use earwax drops first and stuff the ear with a large cotton ball.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let it lie on the same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out due to this, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If it doesn't jump out, take many small and light pebbles according to the size of your finger and heat them slightly in the fire; then make the patient put one or more cotton balls into his ear, and press with one stone on one side and another stone on the stone inside the ear; and keep doing this with one stone against another until all water jumps out entirely, and it jumps out completely; if you see, take a string, insert one of the stones in the ear, and hold the other end of the string while heating the other stone until the closest stone is burned; then repeat the process with other pebbles until all the water jumps out, as we have said above.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of small animals, like fleas and similar things, treat them as we have said in the division; but if they are large and can be felt, bring tools for extraction such as tweezers; and it is easier to remove what is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earwigs, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in treating with distillations, it does not help; if there are no worms present, take the thread of this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And insert the most subtle head into the ear according to the degree of pain of the patient, then suck it out completely; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 If they do not come out, stop up the canal with cotton as I said earlier; if they protrude as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the treatment of worms, and you will find or treat the distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear to this extent, it is the shape as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And make a container of silver or tin placed below one small hole, and above it cover with a distiller; and for pressing within the distillation have one device made of tin well-made for this purpose, and if you see take one scraper and wind around its tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you wish in the container, and let it be in the ear; then push down into the scraper with all the cotton and press moderately until the oil is distilled or rises from the ear; and the patient will feel the scent within, and let one spoonful of the distillation be heated with fire as if it were being distilled in the ear; and ensure that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be very good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the earstopping
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without having at least one hole in the ear; and this same thing happens with adults due to an ear infection or puss within the ear, and this ear infection sometimes completely fills the ear, so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small amount of pus discharged from the ear, which can be clearly seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it comes in completely and cannot be seen, it is of grave healing in various positions, and in such a case, you must place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening apparent, you should open it entirely with that spatula as shown here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And should be entirely sharp in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the opening is of flesh or cartilage of the ear, you should hold with subtle tweezers, and strike gently until the cartilage is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the swellings are entirely in the ear, take a fine razor lightly and heat it slightly with fire, then place it in the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the swelling causing pain in the ear of the patient, make a small incision carefully, ensuring not to harm the nerves of the ear; then insert a tent according to the width of the wound and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Apply this daily until the wound is healed, take a linen cloth and soak it in rose oil and powdered vitriol; if you see the ear swelling, then pull out the first cloth and apply another linen cloth soaked in ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling disappears; then heal it until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If there is a flow of pus, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and apply other treatments to remove the flow of pus which are either distillation methods.
de la char des papieres	of the wood from paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is a remedy that comes on paper for the eyes when they are moist and dry; you must stretch them with tweezers and scissors, and then press them with a spatula from their roots; then put vitriol powder on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not work, you should cauterize it with the subtle cautery of the lens and then cauterize after incision; many times they heal, but nothing stays from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Often in parchment come things that resemble hail in shape and hardness, which is why this disease is called "hail", and it consists of a large accumulation of moisture on the parchment above and below; the work is as follows: keep watch to ensure that the hail remains stationary from both sides, for it is easy to know; then make a wide opening, then peel off each side gently, then take with tweezers, and crush.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cover it with a patch and only slightly prick the paper, nothing hurts the patient; if the wound is large, collect it in a stitch, and let it heal until it is healed; if it is small, do not apply too much force because the ointment restores it quickly and causes pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the paper and grab the hail with forceps, crush and press it from both sides; if the paper is moved by the incision, do not worry; when the hail is crushed, apply salted oil and cure the wound of the one who has swelling until the patient heals.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 A liniment called exinach is applied to the papers of children's eyes, and this happens more to infants than adults, and it causes great pain to their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears flow quickly to their eyes; therefore, they lie down immediately and sleep on them, and have their papers under damp cloths that swell and cover the appearance of the exinach which opens in oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your hands and feel the dislocation emerging between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places his head in your hand; and then take one cloth made of linen, and arrange a tent-like circle according to the amount of exinach from each part, then put it over [the eye]; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is collected within the circle; then make a small incision in the moist area with a sharp spatula, but not larger than the wound you would make when opening a vein; and cut the skin completely until you see the exinach; and in multiple positions, the exinach comes from the incision, according to the form of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then hold the cloth tightly between your hands and turn your hand to both sides until it is spread out; and ensure that you do not damage the incision, that you do not reach the oil with the spatula, or that you do not cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the start of the cut, raise a little the incision lightly until it appears; then pull it out as we have said, then moisten cloths in oil and water, and place them on top, and hold with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And for such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal him until he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If an abscess forms at the joint, then heal it with plasters softening it until he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hair of the papyrus (meaning: plants or fibers resembling hair)
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper lice are born with hair other than nature's, and they are raised, they harm the eyes, and bring on kinds of diseases such as habitual weeping and swelling of the paper lice and albugine, all due to the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to cure them: either by cauterization with fire, or by medicinal heat as mentioned in the previous chapter on cauterization, or by incision and stitching, or by caustic substances, as I shall explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper lice from the oil onto your left hand; if it changes color, that is good; if not, push a needle through one filament of it; and remove the margin of the paper or where the hairs grow from those hairs, taking one filament across the whole paper, and shave it; then make an incision in the part beneath the paper, under the hairs adjacent, covering the whole spatula, from the large tear to the small one; then pull one filament, and place a small tent of cloth and linen under the paper, then mark on the paper a hook-like figure, like a mirte berry, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity with which you intend to lift the paper as previously designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And if there is need for much paper as the paper is softened; then spread it all over the plaster on the two lines you have marked, starting from the large blister to the small one; and let one of the cuts be near natural hair growth in the thickness of a root, then insert the onion into one of the two corners of the wound, then peel off all of it; then bring together the edges with a sewing stitch using a thin woolen thread and squeeze out the blood, and add adhesives to the excess threads on either side as necessary; if you wish to do this, but if not, leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then heal the wound without stitches with drying and constricting agents, because the paper lifts away from the edge of the wound and the assembly, but the stitches are spoiled (as they say in ancient times), and this is work without fear; and there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a shape similar to the leaf of myrtle, as we have said before, with three onions separated according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut that which stands above the small sections equally according to the following form:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 If you do not have the ability to hold the pliers, and the thing is not even, take a needle with thread, and insert it through the figure; insert the other end of the thread through the large incision, and the second end through the small one, and arrange the threads equally between your fingers; then move your hand equally, and pull up all the skin as you have described; then suture the two edges of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments; sometimes the hair from the wound turns white: in this case, use what we have said about the incision; but the suturing in one place and another is more complex.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of canines is as follows: you should fold the paper and place it inside as I have said, and then make two canines by hand, and two thin stitches equally long as the paper and the width of the spatula; take the two heads of the two parts where you hold the threads; then carefully assemble the one above the other on top of the paper covered with oil, and bind the two canines of the two parts together; leave it for some days, and the skin that is tightened will rot and die, leaving a hole through which pus can escape.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it takes a long time, if he strikes with force, then heal him until he is healthy; and when the wound heals over, and the paper is lifted, and the hair will not grow anymore; these are the shapes of the two dogs you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The tasks are such that you take a fine needle, and tie a thin silk thread to it; then assemble the bones carefully and join them delicately, and make sure the lengths of the threads form a palm's length; then prepare another thin silk thread briefly, tie its ends together; then place the patient's head in your hand; expose the work area to sunlight so that the task is clear, for it is a subtle and delicate procedure; then push the needle into the hole where the hair is alongside, and make it pierce through the skin hastily but not through the natural skin; then pull out the hair up to the assembly, and push the pulled-out hair into the assembly, if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then pull your hand until the hairs come out entirely with the natural skin.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the bones are treated and the hairs do not come out with them, you will pull out the bone with the thread that you have prepared, until the bone emerges from the wound and can be seen through the oil; then pull out both the bone and the thread, close the wound and leave it for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh heals; if the hairs are small, take a long hair from the head naturally and let it grow with that one, until it is elongated and then cut it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purulence of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "leucorrhoea" or the purulent discharge comes in the eye, it can occur in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens due to a sudden wound, or incision, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the method of treatment for this is that you open the wound, separate the lips of it, and put in tents of linen, and let it heal until it is healed; and you must not use anything in its treatment that dries or constricts.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 If you do this, the disease worsens more than the first; but of things softening, such as fenugreek; and the rose of water or oil and flax seed cooked, and immediately after it dissolves in any oil, and wraps it in a tent, and cures with it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the secret of your cure is that you must not suture it in its previous form; and this work that we have mentioned is not far from correcting this disease, so that it does not return to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This disease which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterizations and similar things; and the method of work in it is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and pierce it into the flesh, and make it go through both cheeks of the flesh; then place the flesh on top of the whole needle, and strike with a broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it should, that's good; if not, take the rasp and put it in the crack, turn the paper, and make two cracks where the inside of the paper bends; let the joints be at the ends of the two cracks, forming an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter with the name "Greek"; then remove that cartilage, according to the thickness it bulges out from the paper, and then join the two separated parts with a linen thread; then apply the medicine for softening as we have said earlier, and bandages, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the sickness comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, then you must make a clean incision under the hair on the paper, as described above; then squeeze between the two leaves of a glove, as I have said; and the work should be done according to the shape of the illness, for it is very diverse in form; and wise masters prepare all kinds of devices with every possible means to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what work and instruments are needed in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	under the skin of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this type of suture occurs in a man's hand in such a manner that the paper above is sewn with white oil, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must press the tip of a razor blade beneath the paper and lift it up; hold it with pliers until you extract the substance from the spatumile (a thin, delicate instrument), which should not be too sharp or too jagged, so that the patient does not suffer from the overly sharp spatumile that might hurt the oil; and make your incision, from which you remove the assembled tissue, gently, so that the paper returns to its natural form. The entire assembly is then healed, and sometimes in the oil it becomes infected, with acid and pus; then place a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and put wool moistened abundantly with egg on top of the oil. After three days use colloids and healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail has two kinds: one is nerve-like and resembles a hard horn, and another that is not nerve-like but resembles white congealed moisture; when it is touched by iron and cooked with tweezers, it cannot move; and both look like they are beginning towards the great lachrymal, and grow little by little until it covers the entire eye and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then you open the eyes; take a piece of paper in your hand, then pick up the nail with tweezers of small double curvature, and place it above; then take a needle, and put one horse hair or cow hair and strong thread; bend the point of the needle a little and pierce it into the nail, and pierce through the entire needle, and tie the nail with thread and place it above, and scrape all the hair from the side of the nail that follows the lid and the sinew to the hair until the root of the lachrymal, then scrape the remainder in the root of the lachrymal with a subtle spatula and small forceps, leaving the natural tear duct or lachrymal intact; and sometimes the nail is placed on the eyelid only, and at the end, as we have said; then scrape off all the spatumile from which this shape is formed:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep the spatula not to touch the skin tissue and break it, and that the pruning iron is not pierced; and after the incision pour oil a little bit of crushed egg yolk, and from collyrium made of litargyre, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with what is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerve-filled, and you cannot push a needle, and the unguis can't enter, many times this appearance of nail is treated with medicine; and they grow as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, open the oil of the patient, and take the spatula lightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail gently, and if you see that it does not thin out at all and the reason is pressing on it, distill from your mouth into the oil of collyrium made of litargyre and red collyrium and crushed egg yolk, and stop the oil until the next day; then repeat the other work according to this same process, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the oil, like an abscess heals, then milk it, and first heal the abscess hot until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the wound deteriorates in oil due to great harm, then suspend it at the onion, and cut a part of it but not all, so that tears do not come; then distill red collyrium oil made of litargyre.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 For some men, a red pus sometimes arises and covers the nail and remains on paper and turns to the side, resembling a rosebud; and such is the operation that the patient places his head on a pillow, then he opens the eyes, and everything should be cut away correspondingly, and hold it with force; then make the first cut, and go on cutting to the edge until you reach the end, but be careful not to pierce the oil at the work; and it should be an incision with the spatula as we have said in the nail incision and the small forces of what one uses to remove the nail bed, as shown by this chapter's form; and when the incision is completed and all the pus is removed, apply the oil of turpentine or you distill red colloid, or medicines resembling corrosives, and put cotton with egg white on top to ensure that it is well sealed; and if anything remains, the patient should be covered with a dressing, and if you doubt that it is well sealed, leave the oil and treat the abscess with things soothing abscesses; then return to your work until it is healed, and do this for all pus that is filled in the oil by such means.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you dilute the treatment of each oil with natural oil and an accidental way with iron work, and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is strong enough to bear this procedure.
des voines des eulz	The veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 Red veins that are covered with oil become visible and their work (operation) can be seen and the oil weakens completely every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Then it is necessary for the first thing to be done that you look at the oil where the problem is, and ensure there is no other disease except the swelling; then apply heat as follows: instruct the patient to place their head in your hand, then press those veins all along the affected area according to your wisdom, and make the incisions subtle, double, as shown in this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two degrees of pressure in one stroke according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then gather the veins delicately and squeeze out the blood hour after hour until you see them move away from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the points of the spatula, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that you don't cool the veins; and when you have done this, if it distills green and red oil, it will correct those who are clotted.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	If you cannot collect all of it in that hour, make a poultice with soothing things on the oil to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is relieved and the abscess is certain to heal, then continue according to this method as before until it heals; and this is the form of cauterization:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil duct
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not cured, there is a defect in it that you should incise above the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then repair it with all the instruments mentioned here; it is called "rough head", and it should be made like a new head, pointed like a limestone as shown in the following figure:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the corrupt bone on its base, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is crushed; do this once, then restore the location of medicinal extracts.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the joint is welded and pus forms around it, and the body of the bone is welded, and remains so for 40 days without healing or abscessing, and no bad accident occurs, knowing that it is healthy; if not, there is no other remedy but to bring the fistula back to the neck as follows: you must uncover the bone again with an iron, and with medicines that burn, and when it is uncovered, take a foret according to this form, and the tip of the iron should have three angles, and the shaft should be tapered towards the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 Then place it on the exposed bone of the socket, and move your hand away from the oil hole, then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it if they hold their hand on their neck; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the joint, the matter goes to the neck; it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the flow of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are widely open and do not close of their own accord, you should hold the patient down; then clean them, apply mustard or honey without piercing, then put oil (made of acacia and aloe, incense, and sarcolocola) on it, and hold the oil in place with bandages and cloths. The type of cloth to use is such that you take soft cloth, fold each one into four, and place one on top of the other according to the amount required by the eyes; then hold them together with a firm bandage, and continue applying mustard or honey without piercing; then remove the mustard or honey and leave the oil in place for a day and night; if the oil becomes soft, you should tighten it more; then remove the oil after a day and night, and if you see the eyes healing, that's good; if not, continue applying the oil and cloths and the bandage until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The open wound of the eye does not heal on its own.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the cloudy eye, it becomes like grains of resin and is visible to see; then if you see it covered, the remedy is as follows: take an awl and insert it into the root of the affected part up until where you want it to stop, then insert another awl or thread doubled at the tear duct; and make it pierce, leaving the first awl in place according to its position; then tie a piece of thread around the eye socket and tighten it, then remove the awl and put oil-soaked linen on it; leave it until the filaments grow with the eye, cure the oil with soothing things until the wound heals; sometimes the wound is held in place by the eye itself with a circular piece of cloth around it until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear swollen, pierce them with a thin spatula coming from pure oil, clear the pus, and close it up immediately; then draw it out when it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	with a thin spatula coming from pure oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is not fever but an inflammation in the oil, resembling a boil that descends; and the appearance of the work is such that you make the patient sit on the prepared seat and upright, then take hold of their head with both hands, move it until you see the inflammation come to the surface at your eyes; then let it be pricked and do not drain and uncover the light; let the patient see things as they are accustomed; and if it does not drain beneath, know that it is an abscess, and if the draining of the boil is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Have the patient sit between your hands, then take the thin spatula and place it on the corneal membrane and the cornea, along its entire length; and when it is protruding, distill into the sharp hot oil mixed with honey, or hot oil boiled with fenugreek and honey. Then treat it with another cure until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	The sharp points of oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have the resemblance of the eyes in the division, and what is necessary for piercing; if it works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 You must have the patient sit cross-legged, away from sunlight, and hold the oil close to the eye and squeeze it very tightly; then take the paper of the oil in your left hand if the eye is on the left side, or in your right hand if the eye is on the right side. Then with your other hand (opposite the injured eye), take the instrument called "almagda", and touch the point of the instrument to the cornea along the thickness of a hair, in that area of the oil near the lower eyelid. Push the instrument named "almagda" firmly into place, hold your hand steady until it pierces through the cornea, and feel that "almagda" enters the empty space; and the measurement of the path of "almagda" should be at the full length of the space from the pupil to the end of the iris. This is the cornea of the oil. You will see the bone in the paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then push the instrument to the bone or the eye socket, and express it through another hole afterwards.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If the instrument is to be applied now, the patient sees it before him and the tool in its oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After a short pause, and if the instrument rises again through the second passage, place the force with the tool, and when it is fully inserted and does not advance further, move it gently around your hand little by little; then put in another small amount of gem oil from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then, moist a cloth or woolen cloth with rose oil and egg, and bind it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, place on top, finely ground with much egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the oil due to its hardness, since there are some men who have excessively hard hairs, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 Therefore, pierce the conjunction only and do not advance too deeply, but make it subtle, then insert a little, as we have said; and when the work is complete, arrange for the patient to sleep on his back in a dark room; and be cautious of all movements, take light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and tie him according to his position until the third day; then untie him in that same dark room, test his sight, and make him see some things, and then re-tie him until the seventh day; it is not necessary for you to do this during the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you loosen him, because the instrument rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If an abscess swells up, you should lance the oil before the seventh day, and direct it to the one who soothes an abscess; and when it is appeased, you should close the wound and put over it a dressing for any number of days, and remain in that darkened house always.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 Then depart from the house slowly and gradually, and turn yourself to your cases; and know that no disciples should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that in his country, people do almagda piercing, which causes the water to come out, but I never saw anyone with it in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they should be specifically:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And these are the characteristics of the heads of this same subtlety, and the rear parts in four corners sharp.
de la char sor le neis	of the pus in the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes there are born or are born charred abscesses of various kinds, and some of them seem to be like scorpions with many points; and if there are such as it has an ulcer of darkish color, and if the char is swollen with a whitish color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case of the patient who is weak and not stiffened, it is necessary that you make him sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and pour the onion juice into those parts, and pull them strongly; then take hold of that which you can support with the sharp, thin spatula on one side, until you know that the char is completely dislocated.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be held, you must cut it all off with delicate instruments gently, so that nothing remains; and if without being cauterized or bandaged, the abscess bursts, the remedy is as necessary; and if these are malicious abscesses, you should hurry and burn them with cautery until the pus is drained and all the sores are removed, then pour oil of roses or vinegar on the wound.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the dislocated area is not opened and moisture comes up to the mouth, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that a char is born in the bone above, so the instrument does not come to cut: then you bind a large cotton thread, soft and moistened by hand, with a space between each knot of about one inch or less; and put the patient's shoulders on the thread through his nostrils as far as he can reach, and pull in smelling until it comes out through the nose into the mouth; and children at school perform this many times, and it is easy for him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know each other in turn as we who are present.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do as you know that they have corrupted the flesh, then pull out the filth, squeeze the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the wound as before; do this for 3 days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; and then put a plank bandage on it for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the shape of the instrument to purify the head, as one distills oils and medicines into the nostrils.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or brass, resembling a lamp with an open neck, like a cane, and lead it in the same way; and if you see, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the pus in the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times, a disease called "telul" arises in the head of the neck and grows larger and larger until it can be seen with the eye; therefore, you should cut it at the beginning, and boil it completely, then put the cautery or burning medicine on it; and if it is delayed to be cut when it is large, take care if it is hard, of a reddish color, and has poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an enlarged abscess, for when it is cut once, much harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft-touched and not of reddish color, you can cover it completely; empty the patient and cut cautiously, cure the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when solution comes in one of these articular cavities [joints], it benefits little, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when this happens to anyone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then place the two lips together in a stitch, heal it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated from one side and the other, you must scrape all the parts of their edge until they heal, then place the two lips together in a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood, and incense ground; and put some plaster of strong or other plaster over the powders, and leave it until it dries up, then heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the stitching is such that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the abdomen stitching; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	about abscesses from lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Within the lips there often arise hard abscesses, resembling grains of wheat, both small and large; then you must turn the lips, and cut above each tooth, and take it with forceps and crush it in each part; then apply the lee of vitriol ground, until the wound is cauterized; and then anoint the wound with oil of asafetida, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the jaws
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.
