Often a swelling arises on the jaws, which the ancients called "albulus"; you must hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, leaving the wound open; then apply vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders to it; if the swelling returns after incision, which often happens, cauterize it again; it will not return after cauterization; and these are the shapes of the instruments for cauterizing.
des sordens	Of the sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are ulcers in the roots of the teeth inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and harsh; sometimes the teeth become black and yellowish and decaying, when corruption comes to the gum, and they stink; you must have the patient sit on your lap, with his head in your hands, and remove the sores or the decayed teeth as far as possible; then clean the blackness and greenness, and the yellowish and other impurities until they are purified; if you remove that which is at the root, it is good; if not, start again on the second or third day, until everything is cleaned; know that teeth have different shapes of instruments for cleaning, according to what the work shows, because the person who cleans the teeth has other shapes than the one who cleans between the teeth; and these shapes and others are provided with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay the drawing for as long as possible, for this should not be done at all; because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to shave it off.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Therefore, when the patient is forced to draw, you must be sure of the correct tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the patient feels pain and thinks it is a toothache, and draws out the good tooth; however, the pain does not go away until the bad one is removed, for we have seen this happen with saints; when you are sure about the tooth needing to be extracted, you must make an incision around the tooth with strong forceps to protect the gum from all sides; then grind it with your fingers or fine pliers at the root and root tip, until it is completely loosened, then tighten the pliers; and hold the patient's head firmly between your knees so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After the tooth is extracted correctly to break it, and if it does not come out freely, take any of these instruments and gently push it from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, it is necessary to fill it with bandages where the hole is; and gently hold it closed with tweezers so that it does not break when closing; and very carefully work around the gum line to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, or the patient will suffer greater pain from the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And be aware that you do not act like ignorant lords who in their haste and boldness break the cart (tooth) sometimes, and do not bring what we have mentioned; instead they bring a great disease for the roots remaining or for the cart they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled out, wash the area with wine or vinegar and oil; and if blood flows from it, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol (or causticum); and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the forceps, which first silence the teeth, should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you separate the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should be large enough so that they do not bend when separating, and should be made of good iron, and serrated for holding onto the teeth.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains torn out, you must put cotton moistened in butter on it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the limbs are ground down, then put the tongs called "algefri," which resemble tweezers, into it to make it look like a beak of an arrow; and inside, they should be shaped like a chisel, and that is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, you must uncover the entire cheek around the root and use the instrument called "althali," which is known as plier, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be large and thick so as not to break, and if the root jumps out through them, that is good; if it does not, help with all tools, from which the shapes come later.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And help with this tool having two prongs, of which this shape comes from it:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other iron objects that are in front of the teeth roots, and with this tool resembling large pliers, from which this shape comes:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument must not be able to break, and know that many dense instruments are; and likewise other instruments, which are not counted; and wise masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their work and the sickness require, for there are various diseases in which the ancients did not teach an instrument; and if it breaks the chariot or other bones, which it should not, then seek the instruments that are required, as I have said, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be thick and firm to hold the bone so that it does not slip away but can be held and removed; and then restore the joint with appropriate medicines, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, use the entire instrument for that purpose:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural shape and are misshapen, especially in young women, you must know if the root is not near the tooth, and it is not in its proper position, and it cannot be straightened or filed. In that case, extract the tooth; and if it is erupted with the tooth, take the instrument as shown in the figure below, which resembles a small beak, and is made of sharp iron at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth, little by little in many days, due to hardness of the dentin, and because you cannot move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, file it with a small steel file as shown below in form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is similar to the file used for making needles; and with the file, file the tooth little by little in many days lightly, so that it does not move until it becomes smooth; then flatten it at the end with any smoother, and if the dent is too sharp and it bites the tongue, you must file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth fall out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth loosen in front, whether by falling out or being struck, and the patient cannot force it back with eating, and you treat them with medicines that restrain it but this does not work; then they must be held with a gold thread, as silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes; and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth moving towards each other, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the pliers between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, as long as you can do it carefully; then continue covering up to the part where you started, hold your hand delicately and carefully until it does not move anymore; and tie the thread at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then pierce the shoulders with a needle and attach them, and put them back in place between the healthy teeth so that they do not puncture the tongue; and leave it as tight as it can remain, and if they dislocate again, or the sutures break, tighten another thread; let it remain tight and serve for as long as possible, and this is the shape of the tooth and the configuration of the adjacent teeth, and the arrangement of the molars, as you can see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the teeth fall out and are put back in place repeatedly as we have said, let no one intervene who is not skilled and patient; and sometimes they make the shape of a tooth of cattle bone, and place it at the location where it is missing, and tie it in place as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue naturally, or due to an accidental wound; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold their head in your lap, and lift the tongue; then pierce the nerve ligament with a large needle, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it is tough or not, and it is due to an injury, put the cautery and pierce that ligament; but make sure the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is underneath; and when you have done this, raise the limb in warm rose oil or warm cold water, then put a linen tent under the tongue of the patient; and keep them in tension each night so that it does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if blood discharge occurs, put it on the level of vitriol powder; and if it becomes flesh-eating, apply the slow cautery (longguinoit) which is good for this purpose; then treat it with another treatment until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a small, black or hard color that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, pour vitriol powder on it until it burns, then return to your work until you drain everything; then lift up the swollen and inflamed area with warm salt water, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes boils appear inside the throat that are called "godath". They are properly called "the two almonds", and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and pale color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 If it is red and the base is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the discharge of blood; but let it be until it turns black, and then you will cut it open, or it would burst by itself; and if it has a white color on top, and the base is subtle, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check whether the abscess has settled down and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in the sun, with his shoulders in a straight position, and open his mouth wide and the servant holds him by the tongue beneath all the instrument, as shown in this form; and it should be made of silver or fine iron like knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue with the entire instrument and see the abscess. Take the awl and pierce it into the almond, pulling it out farther than you can; take nothing from the cloths with you, then cover it with the instrument, which resembles a cork; even if the head is bent, one end to another, and are very sharp, made of iron or copper:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the base with pliers, here is its shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the base with pliers, here is its shape: (continued)
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman who had an abscess that was within the throat, to be specific, an abscess of small size; and I had applied pressure all over her throat so that the woman could not exhale through the blocked passageway, nor eat nor drink, and would have died if it lasted for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had been pressed in by two fingers through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I therefore immediately thrust it [something] into one place, then pulled it forcefully and removed a large portion of the bone; afterwards I reset another place in the other shoulder, opened its mouth and pressed its tongue; after that I thrust it again into these abscesses, and took a part of it, and no more came out than a little blood; and so the woman's throat was cut open, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut off this abscess for a long time; and the abscess cropped up again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I trapped it and cauterized it within the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts alone, and God did what He willed with them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the arm goes back into the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below the large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the swellings under the armpit are eased, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and if it is round and assembled but not long, and it is red or mottled or black, then you should make an incision for it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to the way that I have said, of its thickness and length, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue to the instrument that we have mentioned before; then prick the onion into the eye, pull it out, and cut it at the second stomach that I have said in the incision of the two apples.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And you must not cover any superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you do more, it hurts the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what was said in the incision of the two anemones (or amends), and cure it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 If the patient fears to be covered, then you must use an instrument for the cauterization of his fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of the cautery is hot and sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient places his head in your lap, and then you press his tongue to the instrument that was said in the chapter of cauterization, and burn with live hot coals, so it is not too thick nor too clear; and employ the head of this instrument, which has the following shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a lock of hair or ointment container that the medicament is put into, like a spoonful of cuillier, and place the instrument full of medicine onto the eye; and the patient lies on his side so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine inside, not to the throat and the nose; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it onto the eye until you see that it is swollen and the irritation caused by the medicine has subsided; then take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and push the instrument filled with cotton into the canal above, until the cotton adheres to the eye; do this repeatedly until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. If you have to start the cauterization again, repeat it, and after the cauterization, clean the area around the eye with a mixture of cotton in butter, and wash what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargarismes until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective through fumigation rather than cauterization; if it is treated by this method, take camomile, yarrow, origanum, rue, and fennel or similar herbs, place them all together in one pot, and add water; boil the mixture; let the pot be well sealed with strong clay; and have one instrument with hairs inside the pot as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And it should be silver or tin, and one of the cheeks pushed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the channel, until the eye is mortified; afterward, this often recurs until the eye dries up, and ensure that you do not do this at the beginning of the abscess's cooling down, for many things happen then; and never do this except when the abscess's cooling down declines.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this is not present, take a cane and put an egg white into the head so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; for the egg white will not let the vapor bother the mouth, and it is good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a fish bone or other sharp object lodges in the throat, so you must draw out what you can see and press the tongue against the instrument until you see movement in the object; if it does not open and remains lodged in the throat, make the patient vomit before the food is fully cooked in the stomach; by chance, the object may be expelled through vomiting. Or, the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cotton, or a radish root, or a small piece of dry bread; tie one thread to the sponge and then swallow it; when it reaches the location, it will adhere, and then you draw it out; if it does not come out as mentioned above, take a splint-shaped instrument as follows:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And bend the instrument into a curve towards the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and lift the head high; beware not to touch the epiglottis, let the patient put the instrument in, because he must move or the matter is worsened; if he pushes it down, or draws it out completely, keep the instrument equal until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 At no time is the saliva of the patient, as I said in the division, beneficial through medication; and when it does not help at all, then look at the throat of the sick person towards the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 If you see the saliva, take it away with a very small spoon, or fine tweezers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 If it is not successful, take a heated iron and put it in the throat of the sick person, then push or pull the iron up and down several times.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 Make the patient drink water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, move it around with your hand often; and as soon as the saliva senses the water, spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall down as we have said, soothe the patient with asafetida, at the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will heal slowly.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The method of fumigation is that you take a pot with charcoal in it and cover it with a perforated covercloth, and put the head of the instrument in the pot; then pour your fumigation on it, and the patient puts the head of the snake into his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape but goes straight in; and at this point, the saliva will come out, and if it does not fall down, continue the fumigation many times; let the patient suffer from thirst, eat salted and bitter things, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for it to pass through this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument for treating the nose is such that, when it can be seen, resembles curved tweezers to enter the throat; and it should resemble a syringe nozzle, and have an abrasive tip made of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many resemble abscesses, according to what is recalled later in this book from one and another, and they are different in perforation and in cutting; and it is in two ways that the one resembles itself, and of those that hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is for those that are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses of the head are other than those in the base, and abscesses in the hollow part of the bone are other than those that come at joints, and each should be judged according to its work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the swelling is measured according to its completion; and if there are those that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that come near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When abscesses come to joints and are left until it is purged around them, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may become corrupt, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 If the abscess is in the main member and you delay the puncture until it has matured, it will harm the main member; or if it is at the base and one perforates it before it has died, it is not advisable to pierce an abscess without digestion being completed, except for one that is at the base, which cannot be brought out completely, and should be cut open and a fistula formed; and it will not heal quickly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time for perforating an abscess that has matured according to its completion, and it is when the pain is relieved, and the fever subsides, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and shrinkage of the abscess's head, and other signs; and you should make the perforation where it depends less on the abscess, and where it has opened up; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places or where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those who have swelling in such a member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a charred state, it is better to leave the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 If you pierce it beforehand, the body's heat will follow, and it becomes filled with much pus; and there is a risk of hardening the lips and deepening the opening.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess pierced in accordance with the body's width, according to what the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And you must make small and shallow incisions for small abscesses, deep incisions for large abscesses, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and when dealing with such abscesses where the herbs are needed, they should be covered; when it becomes as cloth, and is soaked, you must do as for babies: and when there are abscesses cut into three angles, and when those abscesses which are treated like a thorn apple, and such abscesses of the armpits; and when there are abscesses where one makes a round incision, and other shapes and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 One who has no head, as with a superficial abscess, it should be pierced completely; and when the abscess is large and has collected a great amount of pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; then pack the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing out crookedly; do this repeatedly slowly, as much as needed, until the pus is all drawn out; even if the patient has weak vitality, or a woman carrying, or small children, or elderly people in decline.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 The sphincter sometimes jerks with the discharge of pus, which may accidentally cause the death of the patient, but do not worry about it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, be cautious of this chapter and when you have pierced the abscess, drain the wound, and check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a large abscess, bring in linen or cotton threads; and if it is a large abscess with much pus, you must insert one thread after the other until they meet; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, shave it around, fill it with old cotton or linen wool without moisture, and bind it for three days; then open it and heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, apply cold water and vinegar, wet the linen cloth, and place it on the wound repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding continues, administer treatment and care, as well as the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter or the wound or abscess is very nervous, you must place hot tents and damp cloths on it; and if it is summer, and the wound is fleshy, you must place damp cloths on it with cold oil or cold water, for three days as we have said, and then drain the abscess and lance it and care for it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And you should know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 For small abscesses coming on the head, our practice is that they are wrapped in cloths, like the one who prunes a vine, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fat and others that have moisture like boils; and there are some that are hard and stony at the cutting, and no doubt exists that the artery does not oppose this.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the operations of the cut are that you try every instrument that is called "intermissory," from which the form comes later, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, they make an incision along its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is evacuated, they scrape without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately if left; then put cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; if not, in water and linen, and use it on the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who are delayed will recover.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then repeat the lint, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know for certain that it does not remain open; then treat the wound with suitable ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 If the abscess is filled with pus, squeeze it according to this shape, longwise; and pour out its contents, and scrape off all the scab from every part, and apply your entire treatment by drawing out the puss where it lies; and if the arteries oppose you, do as I have said before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And likewise treat an abscess that is hard, and cut and heal it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 Cut through the hard abscess and moisten it, as it will be easier, for there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if for any of these abscesses or head there is no moisture, and among those was the abscess that I lanced or head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if one had cut it with anything, one would have made an injury like from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 For other abscesses or heads coming from these places such as the heads of children and roots of ears, they should be opened at all times depending on their location to let pus flow out; and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often this abscess occurs at the neck, and under the armpits, and in groins, and sometimes they come from other places on the body, and they are large and connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 Each scrofula is properly inside its own side, just like the nodule and the abscess of the neck, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 Some contain moisture, and some are malicious and refuse to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the one that you see with good position on the body, and is similar in color to the body, mute from all sides and not connected to either the artery or the vein, and not profound; then you should incise it from above, strip off the skin of each part, place the two lips of the curettage at the incisions as needed, as we have said in abscesses of the neck; draw it out little by little, and be certain that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the spatula not be sharp nor cutting so that the hand does not slip, and look not too far ahead, lest you incise what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to continue, put vitriol powder or some powders that stop bleeding into the wound, hold the wound closed; and leave it until the abscess is soothed and the wound softens and starts to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the wound is stopped bleeding, return to your work until you are done; then examine if there remain any small scrophulas (abscesses), cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 If there is a large abscess at the root of the wound, do not cut that abscess in its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and leave it to drain without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment and heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 If you excise the entire scrofula, you must gather the two edges of the wound and sew them up now because there is no room for excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 You must understand how to cover the root and draw pus, then sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas with excess, pierce there where the pus has accumulated; and pierce it in the manner as previously mentioned, depending on it, then introduce tents with ointment and similar things so that it corrodes what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply healing ointment until it heals.
de squinance	If the scrotum becomes inflamed and swollen, apply a poultice to it made from crushed barley, wine, and oil. Repeat this process daily for three days.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke and wrote about the shape of the throat, but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the slit in the throat called "epiglote" be opened; and no aid should be given by these, because all the veins and the parotid gland of the sick are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in 2 mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the parotid gland, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid the strangulation that comes from the swelling.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 It is necessary that when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it should be cut below three or four small slits across, between the two circles or by the amount of the incision in size, not in the cartilage; and the less should be capable of the section of the epiglottis such that there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat all along, then cuts the muscle until it reaches the chin; and avoids the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cuts the trachea as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the chin that jumps through the broken passageway and by the lack of voice; and leaves the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where there is doubt of strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound with care, and stitch it up entirely to touch the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing until it becomes healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged dead, and the flight has fled.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then you must treat the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, thus keeping death at bay; and for this reason, the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, which may take 3 or 4 days. Then they would command to sew up the wound and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 A maiden took the knife and thrust it into her throat, piercing part of the trachea; I was called to treat her, but found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood coming out of it, and knew that she had not breathed or spoken except through her throat, and the wind was flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurriedly sewed up the wound and treated it until it healed; the maiden regained her voice and returned to her normal state, which is why I say in such cases of the epiglottis not to be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in color of a bluish hue, and it is very common in women; and it is according to two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 The accidental one is also according to two ways, of which the first is similar to a fatty tumor, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; there should be caution, and no force should be made except in the case of the small ones, and it should be proven and searched thoroughly through the incision: if you find it as fatty as a nut, and it does not protrude in any way, if you squeeze it, like you would squeeze a pimple, and pull out all its covering, if there is any; and make sure to seal it well, and heal it as necessary until it is completely healed.
des nous	from us (we)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways of ours exist, which I shall say all their resemblances; and now it is necessary that I tell the entire difference between notch and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Dislocation is heat and fever lasting until the boil has passed and the purulence is complete; then the fever rests and the heat subsides.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With the notch there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the body's color, and begins as a blister, and becomes large; and they are of two resemblances, either fatty or moist, and very much in color like what I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the nose, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments called "entromissoire", according to their shape and the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the method of inquiring into abscesses from ours is that you take a more moist place than you find within the abscess and turn your fingers little by little until you feel the instrument has pierced through; then, according to the size of the abscess, extract the pus and beware if it should break out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If the moisture runs out of a wound, let it be colored as I have said for other abscesses; and if afterwards moisture does not come from the incision, know that it is full, then make a cross-shaped cut and grab it with pincers, peel it gently from both sides, and take care to remove the coat intact with the knot; and if you cannot remove it intact, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If nothing remains, the wound may recur many times; if a small amount remains and does not bother you, apply some corrosive powder to the wound, hold it closed, put warm soothing things on the abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the wound is large, cut it in half, and treat the char that grows from it.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or otherwise is contrary to you and you hasten and apply the vitriol powder, let it lie for 2 or 3 days, until the wound heals, and allow the boil of blood to subside; then return to cover what remains unhealed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Here are the forms of cutting instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three crosses called 'albaret', and one called 'breb', and there are also three kinds for surrounding abscesses with fistula; and they are similar to needles used for sewing shoes, and are made of bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and are more experienced in blackwood for surrounding corbeures of fistula; and they are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the knives are similar to what you see here: large, medium, and small; and some have two handles of three kinds, and others have three handles, each of three kinds; and there are also some with two handles and a single handle only, and they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The first part of the shoulder that they cut is sharp, and those who do not cut it completely are only cutting from one side, due to which the vein or nerve cannot be cut; and these are the intrusive hernias that are repaired by hand, so that the patient does not feel pain at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they are not used anywhere other than in a charnut place, such as legs, arms, breasts, and ankles, and in similar places; and sometimes another instrument is used, resembling fistula scissors, according to this form, for bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And one applies it [the cautery] sometimes to the place that is healthy to close veins and arteries, and sometimes in this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to decay and resemble those of a woman; they remain deformed and swollen, and whoever wishes to treat them should do so according to this form of this line b. until g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then, remove the fat, apply medicine on the wound with soothing herbs, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and treat it until it heals; and if the breast hangs downward, is deformed due to its size as happens in women, split it into two folds above, making one end hold onto the other so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line b. up to line g.; then remove the skin between the two lips, extract the fat, and introduce what was said about suturing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it heals; if it does not heal, or the incision is not complete because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; leave it until it softens the remaining fat and the wound, then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	From abscesses in the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses coming from under the buttocks are managed as hard scrofulas where they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those containing moisture must be cut according to this form, from the line b up to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire hole that is in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and anoint it afterwards until it heals completely.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula (scrofula is a chronic disease that causes swelling of the lymph nodes), then make an incision as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound opens up, apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The severing of an artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is inflamed and the skin above it becomes swollen, there are often abscesses; and this also happens in a burst vein and an abscess; and if one recognizes it by the artery, the abscess is long in depth; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels strained; and when it is due to the vein, it swells outwards visibly; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the joints and angles or at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, the treatment with iron is to be avoided for those at the head and also for those who are bloated due to an artery; they should have incisions made above the skin along the length; then open the groin area carefully, detach the artery from the ligaments, until it is exposed; then insert a needle and pierce it right up to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread as I showed you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then press the intervening area with an intromissoire until the blood clots that is there, and remove the abscess; then apply the cure that consists of a bow, until the ligament bursts; then treat it with liniment until it heals; and if the abscess is due to the opening of a vein, you must dye your hand what you can from the abscess to all the skin, then insert the needle under the area that you hold in your hand, pierce it, and let there be a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, with one of the two ligaments on each side of the needle; and if you doubt whether the threads will knot, insert another needle along the entire length of the abscess at the piercing of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four parts; then press the abscess until the excess clots, then press the excess fluid and leave what is tied; then apply a damp cloth in wine and oil, then give treatments with tents and liniments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses from nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and vein, they come on nerves when wounded, or from too much labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this often happens in the shoulders and thumbs and in all the joints where there are joints, and it is the most painful abscesses, and its color appears like the body's color, and it is in many positions with pain; and when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not fully in the body, but under the skin; and it is quite swollen all over, and does not move forward or backward, neither up nor down, and the one who is in joints should not be covered by iron: perhaps there will be contraction; and he who is in the head or forehead, let the skin be lanced.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and strike at its root; if it is large, suspend it to the onion, peel it, then cut open and stitch up the wound, and let it heal until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Hanging large lumps
