Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes occurs in bellies and nowhere else else, and it is a disease called "funge," resembling mushrooms, with subtle roots and large heads; there are small and very large ones of it; I have seen a man who had two bellies that were more similar to mushrooms than anything else, and they made no difference, and were white, and had thin roots, and were hollowed out, and ran with moisture constantly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed and found one at 18 ounces, the other at 6 pounds, and in the incision you can see that if the patient is wet, the color of the intestine is pale and moist with a thin root; if it is cut open with a large spatula, have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in the thigh there often comes excessive blood loss, if it becomes too great, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made thread, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the thread until it stops the flow of blood, and feels hard to the touch; and if the roots are large, be careful when covering it by the belly, but you can certainly cover half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and take care not to cover the sore which is of a dark color and has poor sensation and milky discharge.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess enlarged, and I will come to treat the scrofula hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the belly is filled [with something]
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of boils comes from cautery of wounds or cuts in the sifac [a kind of incision], and it is on the stomach and among some of the buboes, as happens in other places, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries as described, or from wind; and if it's through the sifac route and through the opening of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and it has diverse openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the rupture of the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when you press it with your hands, it returns, and then it comes back, and by chance if it is sutured, it greatly enlarges at the opening of the wound and due to great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it's due to moisture, it is light and opens well when pressed with the hand, without being constrained; but if it's due to blood, then the abscesses are large and hard, and filled according to a certain quantity; and if it's due to wind, it yields easily, and the work is such that you look to see whether the appearance is due to the blood of an artery or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 It is necessary that you let the healing be.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 If the appearance is of the intestine or belly, you must command the patient to take his bowels, and stretch it out straight, then bind all around the belly; then order him to lie quietly between your hands; then go around the area that you have signed with a spatula, then cut half of the abscess with a large spoon; then tie it with a strong thread or a strong cord firmly, and soak the suture needle in oil; then open half of the abscess stretched out with the thread, and put your finger inside to search for the intestine; if you find it caught by the thread, remove it, and push the intestine to the exit of the stomach; and if you find the belly, take it with the spoon, and cut away the excess; and if the arteries or veins oppose you, go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and put in four sharp pins, and place the needles around what you have made in a cross shape that you are piercing; then hold the abscess in three leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the area as it is until it can heal itself; and cut the dead flesh when it becomes soft and can be cut, then cure what is necessary, and cover the abscess as we have said; and extract the pus or moisture that you find, then cure the area as necessary, and suture the area.
dou chancre	the boil
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have mentioned in the division the resemblances of chancre, and how to treat it with medicines, and how to avoid using iron cure; and we say that chancre begins in marriage, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be shaved like a chancre that is on breasts, thighs, or similar places, and must be completely removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is large and old, it should not be approached, for I have never seen anyone heal one; no one has ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is to purge the patient once with black bile; then let him purge if there is obvious repletion, then cut the patient into one good length for the operation; then shave your claws or chancre and all the hair from all parts, and remove everything that feels nothing from all parts; let the blood flow freely, and be careful of the wound to your hand or anything, and if the discharge of blood makes you opposed to the incision of an artery or a vein, then cauterize until the blood is coagulated; then heal with another cure until it heals.
de ydropisie	dropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have said in the division that the resemblance of dropsy appears in several ways and how its assembly of water is made, as well as the signs of each resemblance, the treatment with medicine and the one with iron: only these two resemblances are exempted from iron; namely tympanites and yposarche, for it is a lethal thing. So, when you treat this dropsy-like resemblance which is called "eclites" with medicines, and its cure does not work, consider if the patient is weak or if he has other diseases besides dropsy, such as the solution of the stomach and similar things; do not touch iron in such cases, for there is doubt. And if you see the patient to be of strong constitution and he only has dropsy itself, and he is not too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lie down the patient straight on your hands, and the assistant presses the abdomen pushing the water towards the lowest part of the back, then take the pointed spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut through from the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And it should be pierced from the second part. Not too deeply that it reaches the intestine when stabbed, and it cannot be beaten; then check if there is a hernia towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision along the third rib on the right side above the navel; and if it is due to liver disease, the incision should be to the left of the third rib; and if it is due to the spleen, it should be on the right, and the patient should not lie on the incision so that excess fluids do not run to that weak side; then pierce the skin with an instrument, and push, and withdraw your hand to the full depth of a nail or less; then pierce the spleen until the instrument reaches the level of water, which is the position of the hernia, then pull it out, and place this instrument in the shape shown here:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it resembles a thin silver cane, and is made of lead or light iron, and has a small hollow in its lower part; and on one side, there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes use to make a pen quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 Above the opening is the handle, so that when the instrument comes to the point of bleeding, then you should now hold the instrument up; empty it then the halfway or one-third part, for if you empty more than necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he falls down, or approaches death; but empty according to its strength and according to what the dispositions of the strength indicate in the patient and his pulse; then draw out the instrument and stop the bleeding, and it is now held back by the cautery which stops the blood that is above the scyphus, as I have spoken, that you perforate in this manner; then use the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient suffering from the bleeding, and draw out a small amount of blood; do this every day, and be careful not to let it persist but a little bit of blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you have doubts about the patient, and leave much water on him, cure him with burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing and in the sun, and anoint him with wine; and heal him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize the stomach, liver, and spleen after the extraction of water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	For stopping the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born who do not have foreskin at all, or the foreskin is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it is necessary to immediately pierce through every spittle very thinly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then place the thin foreskin of wood and bind it and hold for three or four days until he wants to urinate, then remove the foreskin and make him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps there is no need as the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 The patient with a small purulent wound is to be treated with a cloth of plunged linen, as we have said, and it will swell up.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those with the purulent wound not in their place are to be bled, for no one is born with a purulent wound at the tip of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate before elevating their penis; and cannot ejaculate due to the fact that the matter cannot reach the marriage chamber, and it is an evil disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of work is that the patient lies supine on his back, with the tip of the penis and the base as thick as a pen's feather, so that the perforation remains in place as needed; and beware of the flow of blood which comes frequently, and if it happens, stop the bleeding from the injured area, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	boils on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this albate comes in the penis, and it is an appearance of hideous disease; there are both malicious and non-malicious [forms]. You must take them one by one with subtle care, crush and cleanse all of them, then put cotton wool in Egyptian ointment on top, then cure it with fine ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 If the ulcer is malignant, purple in color and weeping, you must apply a fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cauterized it and if the ulcer is at the base of the penis, and has a part inside the skin and a part outside, you must first remove the ulcer that is inside; and when it heals, treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you treat it together, the head of the vein is not always certain that it will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come into its vein and where it joins; it is necessary to cut away all that is black and corrupted, then lay it on a plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranate rinds and other ingredients, then treat it with other treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding comes out, bring the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cauteries help with the following conditions: for bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the vein is corrupted and receded, it is necessary that you pull or lead from the vein a cable made of yew wood, and make the patient urinate; and when the hair grows to the top of the vein where it happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it happens due to injury or abscess, it is then necessary to shave it with a suitable instrument, until the ligaments are separated, and the head of the vein is released from all sides; and if it is difficult to speak about this, it is then necessary to shave it with a small knife at the tip of the vein and the skin; then press very hard between them, and place a thin linen cloth moistened with cold vinegar on it so that it does not immediately adhere.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in that it does not have a constant healing process; nonetheless, when we perform this work of our own will and specifically on infants, it is necessary for us to make the best and easiest work for their salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and healers performing circumcision around one day, using forceps and a new scalpel; however, it was difficult because there were two layers, and sometimes they would cut the wrong one and leave the other below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound is covered, and there is double pain, and during the cleaning of the tip of the member, the point is not always certain; and during the cleaning of the nail, by accident the iron slips, spoiling the work, and many times it becomes necessary to clean it without need and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the amputation which is done to all the chains of thread I have found the goodness of experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Whenever you press your hand, you should make an equal cut all the way through; but the edge of the skin should be well straitened around the flesh; and the method for the first work is that you make the child think, if it can understand, that you tie the thread only around the rod, and then let him play in all ways as he can; then make it straight between your hands, and tighten the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any instrument; then push your hand to the rod and breathe or shout, and draw it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it very well from the filth assembled there, then tie a double thread around the joint, then tie it below the wound with another thread; and hold it by the second loop at the thumb and index finger, and break between the two threads, then untie the knot quickly and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood flow and coagulate, for this is the mudder; and put powder on top and above the powder spread a glue made from egg white cooked in warm rose water, mixed with good fresh rose oil, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the strength for the healing is this: the two shoulders should be tender and sharp, and the shoulders equally as large as the hand.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the healing is when the marrow inside is at the incision; therefore, you must stretch it to your fingernail so that the wound becomes an abscess; and equalize it, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then take pliers and then press.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they surpass three days, and that which is beneath the scrotum swells, leave it until the abscesses have been calmed and the scrotum is lightly opened; cut it as you can move it, and be careful of the part of the scrotum, this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the affected area with healing powder as we have said in treating powders, and if you cut too deeply, it will go beyond its bounds, but it will not harm; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to a stone, or congealed blood, a bowel obstruction, frozen flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that it is retained by the stone which is in the bladder or neck of the bladder, then you must bend the patient over their knees; put their feet on the back, extend their abdomen from the upper part of the back, and hold the patient as flat as possible; and then constrict the bladder neck to express the stone above it, so that the urine is relieved; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you must administer extraction with all the instruments called "syringe", of which this is its form: It should be made of thin light silver tube, like a bird's feather; the nozzle should be about one and a half palm lengths long, and should be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the urinary issue is that you take a double thread, tie one end to the head of the cotton or woolen cord, and push the head of the cord into the syringe; then fold over the excess of the cotton and insert it up to the head of the syringe, then oil or butter the syringe and fill the syringe with water from an egg, olive oil, and cold water; then have the patient sit on the seat, and lubricate the bladder and penis with oil moistened with water and olive oil and cold water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis; then double the penis over towards the anus; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and have the patient feel the urine come up to the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless because the conduit through which it goes is twisted; then tie the thread to the entire length of the cotton cord, and the urine follows the cotton, then remove it, and straighten the urine; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scratches or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is collected there, and you see it distill liquids and medicines, do everything using the instrument called "clepsydra", and its shape is:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the medicines placed there should be such that they stop the worm well without addition, if it can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see your medicines thrown into the bladder, put the head of the syringe in the moisture, and draw while drawing; if you draw out the moisture with the syringe, and then forcefully push it back in; the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient can feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clistere used to cleanse the bladder: this is it.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is of silver or iron, and the head is higher; and beneath it lies the breast or the ribs fall down; then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you have used to cisterize the bladder, then place it between the two breasts forming a good double thread, and heat the moistured bladder over the fire; then insert the head of the clistere into the sheath, then hold your hand above the bladder with all the moisturer directed, until the patient feels that the moisturer has reached the sheath; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly; then force the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like you assemble a thimble, and put in it what you want of oil and moisturer and water, and place it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press your hand until the moisturer reaches the sheath.
de la piere	of the stone (arrowhead or projectile)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stones (arrows or projectiles), and their extraction along with medicines; and I have told the difference between an embedded stone in the body, and all its signs, and when to operate on a stone according to its size; and regarding the bladder, and the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder, resembling a jump in its subtlety; it opens the kidneys, and irritates the patient's penis, and it pains him many times, and then swells; and many foundations come from these jumps; and children's healing is light until they are four years old, and it is very painful in old age, and it is a medium-sized illness to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it often obstructs the search for stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet, bend and move them under, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes upward a little; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downwards; then squeeze and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 If it does not fall to the touch of all, then anoint your left hand with oil if the patient is a child, or moisten with water if the patient is an adult; and push it into its foundation, squeeze the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, press it towards the neck of the bladder; then press hard above, and push it to the place where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upward, and to remove the skin that is below the testicles in the area where the cutting is done; then insert the spatula covering it, so it takes this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And it is to be made between what is between the cheeks and the base, not in the middle but on the left side of the naval; and straight across the back, and your thumb should be at the base or the bottom, and the hole should be wide in front and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance, the pressing thumb that is at the base may cause it to jump out due to pressure; and know that there is this stone or it has angles and edges: if it is round, it is easier to extract; and if it is soft like a plum and round, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then, if it has edges and corners, make the hole larger; and if it does not jump out, you must extract it using tweezers similar to a flat-tipped pliers to pinch the stone so that it doesn't escape; or you push something sharp and thin at its tip; and if you cannot manipulate it in such a way, then widen the hole a little with a drill, and if it doesn't come out, stretch it with vitriol. And if there are more than one stone, first take out the largest at the bladder neck, then hit it, pull it out, and the smaller ones afterward if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 If it is very large, then it must be cut open more widely.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 And there are two things that happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes immediately through the place where the wound cannot heal; but nevertheless you should try to drain it, or break the nails with pliers, as long as you can pull it out in pieces; and when you have finished your work, fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and press down on it, and cover it with a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to cool the abscess; then make the patient lie down on his neck, and do not undo the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen the rope, wash the wound well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of diaphinecon and basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses and corrosions come in the wound and freezing of blood in the bladder occurs, which causes urine to be retained, known as edema with urine: then you must apply pressure on the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to burst; then lift the wound from pus and pus-like material and purify it, and help in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the herbs that you use to cure it, that you bind its two knees together, and apply the medicine on top.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the wound is small and it is conducted by the penis and pierced through, and urine cannot come out; you can cure it by what I say next, that you cut it many times, until the incision is released from this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already experienced this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod of this shape and sharpened at four angles on one tip:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take the thread and tie it around the shaft of the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the awl gently into the shaft, until it reaches the stone; then turn the awl towards your hand in the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured; if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie the thread around the stone from below and the other one from above, then insert the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, pull it out, remove the thread, clean the congealed blood in the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	From a woman's stone (or pelvis)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rarely that a stone (or pelvis) becomes pregnant in women, and if it ever happens, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that it cannot be found a woman well-informed who exposes herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of the man, which requires a more profound incision, causing great fear. If such a case arises, you must take a midwife who knows her craft, and if she cannot be found, cast a subtle probe instead; and present a wise woman in the life of women, or one who knows part of the art, and command her to examine the stone; and watch carefully that the woman is a virgin. Then you must push with your finger or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should press it under her finger, and you command her to push or compress the patient's hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is dislocated, you must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike above the bone at the root of the thigh near the middle of the hip, where the bone moves easily; do not move your finger above or below the bone and make a small incision first; then press on the swelling in the incision, so that the bone protrudes as much as possible and know that there are many types of bones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 know the forms to understand the cause.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the bone protrudes, put vitriol powder broken on it and hold for an hour until the bone stops bleeding; then return to your work, as long as the bone is fractured, and have the tools I told you about in the extraction of bones to help you in your work; and if the bone protrudes again, and it is an artery that is cut, put powder on the site and bind tightly with straps and bandages, do not try again, let the bone be and do not draw it out, for fear the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has been relieved and the wounds have healed, then return to your work until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	Of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery hernia is nothing but a collection of moisture or white matter, which is under the skin near the testicles, containing an egg; and it is called "white matter", and sometimes it properly belongs within the lining of the eggshell, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the leather of the scrotum between the white matter we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the cause of this watery hernia is weakness that comes to the testicles, and the matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes there is a blow to the head and this moisture takes on several colors: it may be turning yellow, or red, or black, or white, and this happens often; these are signs of recognizing this condition, for if it is as white as we have said, it is an abscess, long like the figure of an egg, and do not open the head, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the cloth itself, then the abscesses are rotten with a part of the egg, and for this reason it is believed to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the hide of the sheep and the membrane, one can feel it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe it thoroughly everywhere, so that you may know its form as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, judge what is inside based on the probe that follows.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with iron, the patient must be bled according to our power and the fullness of his body; then lie him on his back, upon something slightly raised, and place many cloths beneath him; then sit to his left, and command the assistant to stand on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the hide of the sheep; then take the spatula, strike the hide of the sheep between them lengthwise until reaching the point of the bone, and ensure that your incision is straight in dividing the hide of the sheep up to the white membrane, and carefully skin it as far as possible; then pierce the white membrane completely with water, and extract all the water, and then put on your bandages, and suture the white membrane upward; and do not touch the bone, but only the white membrane; strike all around it carefully, so that if you do not strike it properly, the water will return; and if the egg bursts during your work, reform it in its place when you have completed the white membrane operation; then assemble the two sides of the hide of the sheep into a stitch, then treat the wound like any other wound, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if the egg (or yolk) is corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you bind the vessels which are suspended, taking care of the outflow of blood; then cut the joint to its entire length, extract the egg, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if an abscess has been assembled into two parts together, know that these are the branches; if you cut the other part as you did the first equally, then squeeze out the blood, and put moistened linen in oil of roses in the wound; and put more moistened linen in wine and oil on the outside, and put the two on the boils, and put drapes doubled over it, and tie it all with a string according to this shape:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two drapes made of coarse linen in this shape and sew them together into the girdle of the breeches, one of the heads takes hold below at the base up to the back, and the other at the part of the handle; and the other two heads on the two sides, and bring all the rest together in the braiding knot; and sometimes this branch of cautery is used instead of iron cutting, and you take a sharp, thin cautery, and cut the skin of the boils, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus from the abscess is exposed; then take the cautery in this shape, and pierce the pus with onion-shaped holes, and scrape off the skin with this hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And strike with the iron in all ways that you can, until it is heated; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg (yolk); and know that this work is more beneficial; and be careful of the flowing of blood, and be aware of the surgeries of cutting; and if something happens against it, or an abscess forms or the flow of blood or anything else, cure whatever happens against you, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 If the patient is afraid and does not want to wait for this work due to its horribleness, you should perform perforation as I told you, and it is when, if you are sure by the signs that we have said that ramice aquouse is present, you make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below the whole spathule wide, and place the perforation along the length of the body; let the openings be large, so that all the pus can flow out; then put cotton over the area, tie it up, and allow the remaining pus to drain out until the wound is healed; and if the white linen cloth does not allow the pus to come out through the opening of the wound, you should insert a pen or the instrument used to treat the pus from dropical patients, as the shape is described before; enlarge the opening of the wound, know that the pus will return, and it will be assembled after 6 months or more, and when it has been assembled as before, the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess in the cheeks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the incision of this artery, fear is present in many positions, so it seems that it is better to leave it [the incision]; and I will tell you the work and the likeness of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Then many abscesses come from bodies, and especially from the kidneys; and this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 This is by excess of sour and acrid fluids, which is spread to the kidneys or by percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and no pain is found, but the abscess is severe; and sometimes an abscess is swollen with pus and stone-like, and of such a color, and occasionally it comes from the artery or vein enlargement.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is from the artery, it can be known by the hot abscess position, when you press it with your hands; and it should not be touched at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 The patient with a swelling of the vein is recognized by his disposition at the expression of the touch of the thumbs, and he can well make an incision on this resemblance, and on other things; it is that you cut the cartilage of the toes, then the egg is above, and the white thread passes through it, and delivers the suspension from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already broken with these things born, then you must pull out the egg and cut it; and if it is in front of the white thread, or in that which is inside the vessels, then you must deliver all that tender part and cut it round.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the navel is located behind the back, you must crush everything and extract the afterbirth as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply the wound with damp linen in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess in the cheeks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess enclosed by a covering resembling a boil, with the softening of the toes, and the patient groans severely when he goes; and the cure for this disease is as difficult and dangerous as that mentioned above, and yet we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the raised seat, then push the suspensioners from the lower waist towards your hands, to all the tools near the penis, and touch them with the master's hands, and stretch them out completely; then cut the spatula wide open in the direction of the veins, until they are exposed, and then scrape it from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then insert a needle or double thread, and tie it to the first point where the vein appears, and tie it directly to the other end; then puncture them exactly, according to the length of the body, and drain the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as one treats an open sore, so that no vein bursts that nourishes the scrotum; for there is no harm in this, and if all the veins swell, you must draw the scrotum to all the veins; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the veins, and they dry up and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the nose
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The occurrences of this disease are due to the section that comes from the wound or the extension on the abdomen in the area of the intestines, for which the intestines descend from that injury to one of the intestinal loops; and this injury is either from the wound or from the extension of it, and these two ways of occurrence are due to many causes: either from a blow, or a jump, or a fall, or lifting heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the wound, are that it happens gradually over long periods and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the full extent, because the wound follows the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the surgical incision, which makes sudden pain appear at the beginning, and the abscesses are various appearing under the skin close to it, and this is due to the release of the intestines and the body's reaction to the surgery.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	Sometimes the intestines come out of the circle and are retained, causing great pain to suffer by the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, there is fear, therefore it is advisable to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the method of work is that you instruct the patient to reinsert the intestine into the abdominal cavity with their hand from within in the wound, if it can be reached; then place the neck on top between your hands and tie the legs; then turn the head upward and cut all the skin of the scrotum lengthwise; then push fingers of the thumb into the groin area as needed to open the wound, making sure that the testicles can come out; then remove the covering fat that is underneath the skin of the scrotum, until the white fat is completely exposed on all sides; then place your index finger in the place where the testicle was, in the place between the white fat that is underneath the skin of the scrotum and the second layer of fat, and separate what is behind the testicle and between the second layer of fat; and move to the right side of the scrotum with your right hand, placing the white fat on your left hand, and lower the testicle towards the groin area; and instruct the assistant to stretch the testicle upward and untie what is in front behind the ligament; examine with your fingers if there is any intestine entwined or hardened white fat, and if you find anything, push it into the abdomen; then take a large needle with thick thread made of 10 threads, and insert it into the back part of the fat, behind the skin of the scrotum; after the groin, cut the hairs that appear from the threads, until there are four threads; then assemble one on top of another in the form of a cross, and tie the fat, which we have said is underneath the skin of the scrotum, with a strong ligament of two parts; then wrap the hairs with thread, tying them tightly with two parts, so that no one of the servants who feed them can enter; and place the ligament according to the first ligament length, and after these two ligaments leave the fat that is underneath the scrotum, leaving a large space of about one finger; and after all around the round shape that the eggs carry; then cut in the part that is behind the skin of the scrotum, until it corrodes and swells, as we have said before; then bring moisture-soaked linen into the wounds and place it there, and place the ligament that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white parts as we have said are cauterized after incision, due to fear of blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this often occurs and leave the ligament until it chooses to break itself; and if it lingers in falling, then sprinkle with hot water, and place what we have said on it until it breaks; then heal the wound from another remedy, until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	Of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone dare to perform a cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like the ramish which is connected to the bone, in this manner you tie the vessels, after cutting them gently below; then smash it in the middle, and treat the abscess from those who operate on it, until the vessels break; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.
