Sometimes a hernia occurs in the anus, as we have said, and do not remove any of the intestines at the anus, and if some are removed, it is bad, and repair it every hour; and even if it remains too long in this place, the wound or sores grows, until the intestines are removed; and this happens by the extension of the hernia which is in the anus, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and inflated the anus and opened; and it is cured by cautery as we have before said; and sometimes it is healed by iron in this way: and it is that the patient lies on his back between your hands, then smash the swollen hernia to a width of three fingers; and then pull out the hernia which is under the skin that hangs down, then take the thumb and place it on the visible hernia; and press it at the abdomen, then bring the two visible parts of the hernia together on the top of the thumb, and press them both; then pull out the thumb, and do not cover or extend the hernia nor anything else as I have told you in the treatment of the hernia of the intestines; then heal it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, if they become soiled and heal the wound, until it heals completely.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The cloth is compressed, without appearance in the wound, and the cauteries are more effective in this place and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin on the buttocks
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin on the buttocks softens in some men, because the charms inside are softened and visible; and when one sees it is necessary to make the patient lie down on his back, and to strike the softened skin with the natural skin; then bring together two lips at a stitch, and if you see, sew the excess of the softened skin at 3 or 4 stitches firmly; then strike between the stitches, and the cure as with other wounds, until it heals, and close the hole with thread.
dou chastrement	the punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that cauterization is mentioned in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary in two ways: the first is when the mirrors (torturers or interrogators) ask a suspect about something related to the wound and its healing; and the second, because we often need cauterization of certain animals for our aid, such as goats, sheep, dogs, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 Therefore, cauterization is done in two ways: either by drawing or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the method of drawing, we seat the animal in hot water until its genitals are softened and relaxed; then we grasp it with our hand, keeping it until it is restored and no longer feels pain.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 From the castration of size: you should dip the animal and press its scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspenzoire, and strike each testicle with a blow, when you have well scorched them; leave any small piece of skin and the subtle one that is on the vessels; this method of castration is different from that made by attraction, because at attraction something from the scrotum remains accidentally, which causes the animal to desire lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism is according to the males in two ways: one way is that between the two scrotums opens as the female figure by nature, having hair and sometimes urinating in court.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And another way it is in women, and there is above the navel as a rod, and they coit.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the healing of men and women is that you cut all the nearby charred areas, and heal them as other wounds; in another way, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of their penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the tenor (modern English)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 A burn adjacent to the natural part is called a tentigene, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have one as large as a hand, and that is healing.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 You must dye the excess of the tentigene with your hand or ink and cut it lightly; do not go too deep, so that there is no flow of blood; then heal it with other remedies until it is healed; and another char that arises from the mouth of the wife, and spits out, and possibly flies away, and resembles a cow, and for this reason they call it by the ancients "kowe disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If you must cut it (the shoulder), as we have said before, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	The erratic growth is a hardened or stone-like tumor on the surface of the body; and it is called "erratic" because it cannot be removed by simple cutting. When this kind of swelling arises in the body, it should be cut open with a knife until it is completely severed from its base; then take a hot iron or an emetic and cauterize (sear) the wound, so that the bad humors do not remain there and cause more pain.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 The erratics (hydrocele) are of two kinds: when the nature of the woman is not pierced, or it is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to disease that comes; or caused by a hard knot, or subtle or thick sclerosis, and is made complete in the womb, in the side, or under it, or anywhere; and they prevent conception, pregnancy, and possibly the growth of flowers (ovaries); and these are recognized by the swelling of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the swelling is close to appearing, it may be at your hand or arm.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If the soft, thin place is near the liver, hasten and proceed as follows: put your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, spread her legs; then form the two livers so that the thin soft place becomes round, and apply pressure with a woolen cloth moistened in oil; then let the woman rest each day until she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the soft place is hard and thick, you must cut it with a tool resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the wound is made of raw flesh, suspend it on an onion and cut it; have the medicine ready, consisting of white wine vinegar, dragon's blood, frankincense, egg, mix them abundantly; then apply a broad strip of flax cloth to the wound so that it does not heal; keep it long and apply a dry linen tent over it; then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when snow falls in marriage (meaning winter), it should be covered in this manner, unless the abscesses are aggravated.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an aggravated abscess that occurs during winter, one should not intervene with fire.
des emorroides	1. Hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins without a cort (cortex?) which is usual, and when hemorrhoids become old they turn into ulcers; and we have said in the division their resemblances, and signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and ulcers, when they are completely in winter and cannot be felt, should not be cured by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those which are at the mouth of winter, can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then stretch out her ankle with pliers and break it at its roots, then sprinkle powdered medicine that stops blood, such as cinnamon and dragon's blood, and similar things; then leave her feet exposed for an hour, then immerse them in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, apple bark, ivy and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If it does not, make her drink dandelion or marshmallow juice with old wine and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess settles down, if it needs ointment to heal until it is healthy; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles raw flesh, so it must be covered as I have said earlier; then let it heal until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses in the womb
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many kinds of abscess come in the marriage (procreation), such as boils and pus-filled abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Therefore, I must speak about the hot abscess that comes in procreation which is not like those abscesses that cling to the testicles; and if you wish to know about the work of iron, see whether the abscess is acute at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and turns red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hurry to pierce, but let it heal as much as the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a seat, or two small seats where he can lean, and support him on his back and align his legs at the parts away from the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and place his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good string; then let the ball move towards the right side, and bring the instrument for opening the abscess, from which follows the shape; and it is necessary that when you bring this instrument, you poke the rod first inside to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters inside of the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt; and it is necessary that you place the nozzle of the instrument above, and mark the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess is opened and it is handled with soft hands, it should be covered with linen cloth; and when the boil is emptied, you must put in the wound moist cotton dipped in rose oil or dry green oil; and place the soaked cotton from the wound to the edge of the scar, and place on top of the scar and over the needle clean moist cotton soaked in vinegar or malves cooked; then cure for two days with ointment afterward until it is healed; and sometimes lift the scar and the wound with clyster of vinegar and honey, and then of vinegar or long-cooked arum lilies and aristolochia; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 If the wound is healed in a marriage (union), it is necessary that you abstain from iron cooking, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 First of all, the woman must recognize the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see her preparing downstream (having labor contractions), and desiring to push out an arrow: then hasten the birth of the child; afterwards, know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it issues from its head, and follows with a second one; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the child comes quickly; for when it descends on top of the head, it is followed by another one, and the marriage (the womb) is emptied of its superfluidities through good cleansing; and this which comes differently does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 It sometimes happens that it comes upon his feet, or the body or shoulders, or hands, or upon the stomach, or back, and it turns by chance on his neck, and in other evil ways; therefore it is necessary for the bailiff to be wise and skillful in these matters, and to avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures on how one should help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes out through its head naturally and the woman gives birth painfully with weakened vitality, she should be seated on a saddle or held by women, and anoint her private parts with oil or fenugreek cooked in oil; then the midwife shall insert the small spatula-like instrument shown here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 Then cut the second birth canal, and strike at its claw until the child within is expelled; and grab the woman's stomach until the child descends, and if it does not descend, you must fumigate her with musk of fenugreek oil of sage; then make her take a purge of condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus will the child now be expelled.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out, you must gently pull them back little by little; and if they cannot enter, lay the woman on the seat, and lift her feet up; then tilt the seat onto the ground, and bind the woman so she does not cry out during the tilting; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child dies, strike the hands with the knife that is placed in front, extract the child, and pull them back equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the issue of the child upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes upon its feet, you must push it upwards; and then turn it little by little until it is equal; then grasp one of its feet and stretch it out little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 The shoulder can leap up to any height when commanded to jump, and it makes the person vomit with fear; if it jumps, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it [the dislocation] is not as we have said, turn it gently until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Here comes the translation: Gently turn it.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 If it does not jump as we have described, then take a powerful emetic such as belladonna, oil of savin, pitch softened, and grind all together in a mortar; put this ointment into the woman's nature and apply it externally; then make her sit in hot water up to her waist; when she becomes soft, have her wear a linen cloth soaked in myrrh, leaving it for an hour; then have her sit on a seat, then have her vomit and hold her mouth and nose closed, and gently press her stomach because the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the birth of the child on its thighs
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the infant comes in this form, place his hands palms down one by one; then lay him on his back and let his feet hang down below, and he should be lying on the bed; fold his hands palm to palm, and then take hold of his hands above the stomach, and remove the hips bones underneath until it is fitted below; if the infant does not come out, take his legs and turn him carefully, then turn the stomach upwards, then place your hands; rock the infant palm to palm; and command the woman to hold herself as much as possible while the infant comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	The newborn child coming out, one hand holds it from above.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to try to return the hand: if you cannot return it, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed, spread her legs apart; then bring the medicine that I have mentioned earlier; if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then try to return the hand; rock the infant as nature dictates, make it cry, and command her to hold herself as much as possible until the infant comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	For the delivery of the child on its neck, have her spread her hands and turn her face towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the servant press his hand, then gently turn it to and fro, and twist it slightly; and when it becomes even, put on it natural mustard paste and oil, as we have said, then command it to move to and fro; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to seize it; and make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way, administer treatment to all those affected in turn.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When the birth comes in this manner, if the afterbirth comes out in this way, emptying the moisture; and if the afterbirth presses against her face and neck, it must be struck from beneath so that it is not retained, and the afterbirth dies; then push the child down, as far as you need to, and command the woman to seize it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the twins' birth
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes triplets or quadruplets; and this is not strange, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two things do not live, unless they are named; I know them, as they multiply and become active due to the one who defines them, which is linked to filth; and sometimes they go out naturally like weeds under a bush, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 If they come out forcefully, treatment should be as we have said, and the remedy should be subtle, quick, and easy to do whatever it is that needs to be done; and do so in a way that is beneficial for healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children  --> multiple children (in this context)
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 They are sometimes formed in the belly (stomach) in numbers one, two, three, four, five, six, or seven, up to fifteen; and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise man, and it is necessary that the remedy knows all this, because such things sometimes happen; do as is required.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you treat the woman for a dead child or a swollen belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained to manual work; if it is necessary that you know whether the woman is of sound virtue, and she has no accident or fear of death; if it is necessary that the woman lies on her back, her chest inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the minister anoints her with oil from two parts, or ties her to the bed so she is not treated in the delivery of the child; then anoint the mouth of the woman with moist oils with musk-scented alum and fenugreek and flax seed, then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and these musk-scents; then insert them gently into the woman, ensuring that they are positioned appropriately; and keep watch to ensure that the fetus is not breached when it descends; if the fingers are inserted into the vagina, or the collarbone, mouth, palate, below the beard, or in the cervix, or near the sides, and if the descending part is at the feet, insert or push gently at the sides and poke at the middle ribs; it is necessary to hold the finger with the right hand, and place the thumb between the left thumb and index finger, and push gently with all fingers into any of the places we have mentioned, until it comes to an empty state; and this is the shape of the finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then thrust against the other joint, whichever one you need to, so that the extraction is equal; and then make it even by moving from both sides, so that it moves out, and the joints should be closed tightly so that they hold, as shown in the following figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 If any part remains, then oil the affected area with some oil and push it in that part, pulling out the other part; if none remains, then move the joint up to a higher level, and do this until it moves completely out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 If one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be returned due to the tightness, you must wrap it around the cloth until it moves completely; then break it at the joint of the palm or at the finger, and do the same with the other hand and the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is difficult to deliver, or if the skull is assembled badly, you must insert a pointed spatula between your fingers, and with force extract the skull; or you may use the instrument called "almidach", from which the form of the instruments or chapter that follows comes; and similarly do the same for breech births naturally; and then pull out the bones with pliers, and if the head jumps out and it is difficult to grasp, force it using a clamp until it splits where there is the more difficult issue; and if it cannot be delivered, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the abdomen or under the ribs, you must pierce it repeatedly until the issue comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on top of the feet, the attraction is slight, and the reduction to the mouth of the bladder is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is located in the belly or the thigh, then you must draw it out towards the folded cloth held with the hand; and making the belly or the thigh, straighten out the moisture within it; and if the other limbs are dislocated, and the joint remains, press the ball of your hand into the hole in the socket, and pull it to the edge of the socket; then press the thumb or finger and pull out; and if the hole in the socket is narrowed due to abscess heat that has come in, you must not force it, but instead apply moist and fat substances; and apply plasters, and apply them with warm softening and moistening agents.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the infant is on its side, and you can make it lie flat, bring it as we have said in the live child; and if it cannot be done, pull it apart by parts, and leave nothing of the posterior part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done this, apply what we have said in abscesses that come in marriage; and if bleeding continues, it should be made incise and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb had killed an infant, then consulted another about it and revived the other infants.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time an abscess came to his armpit and swelled so much that it opened and started to burst.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the treatment, but I thought for a long time and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong plasters with great adhesion, and an bone came out, and after several days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel much, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	It seemed to be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I wish to cut the wound and break many bones as long as the woman is in the best position; and the woman remained thus for a long time, and then a little pus came out from the place; and I have no recollection of this chapter being other than that when masters find an unknown thing, they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring back the dislocated shoulder to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here follows the form of the pressor, with which one weighs books; and in two turnings are the heads of the two levers.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 Moreover, the horns should be thinner than the restrainer, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the rod should be wide, and the edges of the trees, and half a palm in length; and between the two limbs there should be two matching sockets of the same rod, which are closed on both sides, half a palm in length or slightly more; and these two sockets are inserted into the mouth of the mallet to open when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, similar in appearance but thinner and lighter, should be made of rod of ebony or boxwood, like pliers; and for the two horns there should be two matching sockets, as you see, one palm in length, and two fingers wide; and when you want to open the mallet with all the instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her legs hanging down, then insert the two sockets together into the mallet, and hold the head of the instrument under her thighs; then work the handle of the instrument as you did with the pliers, according to the size that you want to open the mouth of the mallet, until the ball does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is entirely sheathed and has multiple similar parts; and when the mirror reflects them, he works more quickly and higher for humans due to their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not hastily prepare the instrument without first arranging it, as its necessity is not easily excused.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold back her lochia (afterbirth fluid), and then make her vomit in order to expel it; and hold your hands at her mouth and nostrils; if she jumps due to this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If it does not work with the fingers or a spatula (spoon), use a mortar and pestle or a bowl, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the woman, such as rue, anise, chamomile, calendula, centaury; these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put a tube or spatula from the pot, and the other end into the woman's mouth, and hold it until the vapors enter her; then make her vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second one jumps quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment, and does not heal as commanded, instruct the woman to moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or musk oil from aloes, then put it in nature, and search for it; and when she has found it, take and stretch it gently straight, so that the husband does not resist at extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; it will come out and disengage.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 If the opening of the husband's mouth has been stretched, we have said the cure for emptying and fumigation of herbs; and if it does not improve as we have said, make sure you do not pull too hard; but the person who is at the opening of the husband's mouth, tie him to the woman's thigh, then clisterize with ointment formulated from four ingredients; he will recover and heal; however, when she does recover, if a bad smell comes from her stomach and head, and burns the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary to use suitable fumigations for this purpose: no one of the ancients has proven fumigation with dill and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used for fumigating a woman to retain flowers and afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it looks like glass, and they place the head in its natural position, and the shoulders broad above the fire; and let there be fumigation over the coals, and the tinder until it is burnt, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	To drill the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but it has been stopped up with a subtle stopper: therefore, you must pierce that stopper at the right time, and do not pierce it with a sharp spur, and guard the passage so that it is not touched; then place moist linen on it and let it be treated with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not recur, put or place a plum stone there, and leave it for many days, and it should be removed when the patient is seen to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this plugging of wounds or abscesses occurs; it is necessary to cover the wound in this way: if it heals, as we have said with a plum stone.
de la fistule dou fondement	From the fistula base
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come below the foundation are nodules, and those that come out of the foundation defect or in the space between two parts, be it one fistula or more; and when that nodule is old, it is opened, and moisture or white linen or a thin stick is applied to it, and sometimes these fistulas become persisting; and they are recognized by those who know them because of excretion or windiness when the patient defecates, and occasionally there is a jump upwards.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they penetrate up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and they reach the junction of the thigh, and up to the nut of the calf.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one recognizes the fistula at its base, not persisting: and it is that you bite your thumb or base, and insert a fine awl of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 If there is twisting, insert a thin cannula or horsehair until you feel the cannula or hair at your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and no purulent discharge or wind or worm comes out, as we have said: know that it does not perforate; hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates up to the bladder or leads to the conduit of urine, if it shoots out urine and cannot be sealed with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is perforated up to the knee joint, the cannula comes to the level; if there is no twisting and the pain subsides around it, it is that it has already healed, and no medicine or poultice helps for anointing; and in these fistulas pus-producing there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of foolish men who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In one who is not a persian and not old, in hope of health by fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and bends the legs up to the thighs, and has the thighs inclined towards the abdomen; then thrust a probe made of iron or wood, if there is curvature, until you know where the dislocation comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels the dislocation around the base, then you must push your index finger into it, and if it moves, the probe has pierced through it; and if you find that it is hollow or soft, know that it is a persian; do not stir it anymore because it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 One must say that some can be healed well, but this happens rarely; and the aid that one gives, it is this: one should heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as previously stated; and push it all hot into the fistula, until it comes out from the base; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charred things are burned, which are similar to a feather of a bird; and then cure it with moistened tents in butter, until the char is extinguished, then cure it with an ointment soothing and healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it can be healed well, that's good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 But if it cannot be healed otherwise and the fistula is entered and not pierced until reaching the base, and between your finger and the fistula, place a thick covering of char or syfac; and you will see the fistula under this covering with care; when the fistula is covered by the handkerchief, press from the beginning of the fistula and push towards the fistula, then apply the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the end of the fistula; and the fistula will be released, and charred; then burn those charred things that resemble a feather of a bird, and there should be no remainder.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the bone breaks through [the skin], and pierces you, either burn it with fire or apply a medicinal cure.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 The cautery of fire brings about two good things: the burning of these joined-together objects, and the stopping of blood and removal of moisture; then it cures wounds soaked in liquid tents (boiling animal hides) or crushed hay, until the flesh is well cooked and the objects are burned in the coals; then it heals the wound caused by hot iron that has been plunged deep into hard bone, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When it is reset, it heals and does not dislocate again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	If a fistula comes up to the surface of the foundation and is separated from the body, push your thumb or the foundation into it and probe it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent, and between it is the cloth or lining or the objects ready to be pierced, if there is no way of trust or hope through the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you strike deep until bottomless, or if you can, place tents and heal as previously described; and do not go too far that you cover the containing element holding the foundation, let the expulsion come by its own will; then heal as previously described; in case it heals, remove that covering and clean it after it has been struck away from the foundation, either by tent or by another instrument pointed; then uncover the pus-filled wound that is in the area distant from the foundation, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the area distant from the foundation: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you bite the tent into the fistula, and it is where it protrudes from the bottom of the skin above, then take a pierced tent at its head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And put .i. thread twisted in .ij., and push the tent peg through the entire length of the thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it protrudes at the edge of the bottom inside, then draw out the thread from that hole, thus bite your tooth or base, and pull the head of the thread, align the two holes together, compress one against the other, leave for a day or two; repress it once, until the threads catch those charms (or foreign bodies) between them and close; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open by itself, make it open in all possible ways as you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is not advisable to cover a wound with a plaster while it is healing, as previously mentioned, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the spiked spatula used to make a fistula is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, because it should not touch what it should not touch, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids   (medical condition characterized by the swelling of veins in the rectum and anus)
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Emorrydes (emorrhoids) are of two kinds: they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and on the outside there is blood, and there is one or more of them, and they are displaced from their foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are displaced have a little moisture, and in addition, there is a little citric acid or blood, and they have the color of the body; and the treatment for these that are within the foundation is that you instruct the patient to strain in order to evacuate in chambers, until the foundation dissolves and this appears to the son; if you hurry, and place it with pliers, or hold it with your nail, then strike at its roots; and if the fingers cannot hold it due to moisture, take a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camel's hair; and bind them with your hands, then strike, and sprinkle some hot powders on it, as in the chapter about cautery, unless you cauterize it as described there; then cure them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the foundation cannot dissolve, clisterize the patient with a biting and harsh clisterium to clean that which is the foundation, so that it can issue openly; when the patient complains, and the fingers have left the foundation, the treatment is easy; and it is that you grasp them with your nail or pliers, strike them, then cure as we have said, until they are healed, and the patient fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You must apply the stitching in this manner: Take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread above and pierce the needle from another side, and twist the two ends of the thread below the needle, making it loose; and hold the thread tightly, then knot the thread, and pull out the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving some space for the excess blood; then put a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or pine resin on the wound foundation and command the patient to rest; then let it heal until it is drained, and when they are healed, you should treat them with ointment and other cures, until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	With the drying of fevers or foundations   (It seems there might be a mistake in this line as "dou sechement" doesn't correspond to the context provided.)
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is a drying of fevers in the intestines and due to natural constraint; and when the disease is old and medication has no effect.   (It seems there might be a mistake in this line as "sechement" doesn't correspond to the context provided.)
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you cauter with a spatula or your fingernail the bark above, which does not allow it to become moist; then heal it until it dries as required; and if it cannot dry, repeat the shaving more strongly than before, as much as it heals and becomes scabbed; then heal it until it is healed.
dou fremit	The trembling / shuddering
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 Formica (ant) is a small appearance that often passes through the body, and sometimes it freezes the flesh, causing the same sensation as death of shivering, spreading throughout the body, especially in the hands more than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is that you take a cane of an ostrich feather, or a strong vulture quill, and place the cane on the shivering, until the purple circles surround the shivering; then turn your hand around the entire cane while you catch everything around the shivering, and push it through, and remove the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a cane made of iron or wood in the following shape, and be thin underneath and wide above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not perforate, because one must hold the breath and press; if you wish to cauterize, then cauterize the trembling, as is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the clyster (enema)...
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they make an enema of silver or arsenic, or melted beeswax or honey mixture; and sometimes they prepare small or large instruments according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, it is applied in the treatment of children who are weak and suffering, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cluster is either small or large, where the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And it should have an opening where the abdomen is sewn shut, as you see, and the shoulders should be pierced from within; and at one of the sides there should be two holes, and in the other one; and let the abdomen or womb receive the medicines of a beast's bladder or parchment, and let it be pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be a space; then insert strong thread through each hole, cross them at X or wherever desired around, and assemble the abdomen like a purse; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then cleanse (it). This is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the clister with oil or goose fat, or similar thing, then insert it gently; then the servants should examine it with both hands until it is all visible, then remove the clister, and tie the legs of the patient to the bed, and if the medicine comes out, let him hold it as much as he can; and if he sleeps all night long, it will be more help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you plaster the patient with a belly disease of discharge, and the medication begins to heal quickly, continue to treat it until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoids are ulcerated or abscessed, the enema should also be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle enema where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds  (plural of "plaie")
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we shall tell you the treatments for hands and medicines, according to completion.  (The first two sentences are a summary of the previous section.)
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what kind they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are due to piercing with stones, cuts from swords and knives, or spears or arrows or similar things; or those that are done according to the body's organs, such as a wound on the neck, head, back, abdomen, liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, starting with the simple wounds of the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes or a head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is due to an arrow or similar things, and the skin is torn completely and the wound is large, and you doubt whether there is an abscess formed: make it drain immediately from the same head itself, even if blood comes out from the wound, and let it drain contrary to the injured part; and relieve the patient of the fullness of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it does not want to drain, reduce the food, do not drink wine, nor eat meat; and place on the wound if an abscess forms there, soft cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in vinegar steeped; and if no abscess forms, place on the fresh wound, with all its blood, and not moving by air, a powder that I will say a little later; and if fire has moved it, place some ointments on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like the size of a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by suturing, as I will say about wounds in the abdomen, by suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone, gaping and not staying closed, close it; then treat the wound with medicine, put hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large foods such as cooked heads (testes) and grains like wheat, as well as similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if the skin rots and does not reach the bone, close it all up and let it heal on its own. If there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be stopped with medicine, then try to tie it off, and if it dislocates, tie it with a thread; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if the wounds are small and simple, the healing is easy: it is that you put this powder that hardens as soon as the flesh has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of live coal, and grind it finely, and apply it to the wound, pressing it firmly until it purges well and joins with all its blood; then tie it tightly, and leave it to heal, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at times this is done only with coal when neither incense nor dragon's blood is available, but the wound has not yet healed.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the fire has burnt the wound, certainly do not apply this powder; but put on some digestive ointments or wheat flour made with water and honey until it heals, until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the bone fracture comes with a small wound, extract it using subtle forceps; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	About the wound of the neck (or throat)   (I am assuming that 'col' here means 'neck', but it could also mean 'throat'. The original French term is ambiguous in this context.)
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes or affects the neck and it is simple without any difference from that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the arteries are cut.   (The original French term 'col' is ambiguous in this context, meaning either neck or throat.)
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is nerves, there should be no device except for leaving them to heal, and not placing anything restricting; because this harms the nerves and causes them to retreat; and do not place anything cold on the wound, because the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation with the brain which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as warm water, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked water also in warm water, and other herbs in this manner, and wet them immediately.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, bind it with strips, then heal it until it heals.
