Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and closed and full of pus, pierce it or lower it more; if an artery is cut, bleeding will come out, so stop it, clean it, and cauterize as needed; if the spine in the throat is cut, or if a nerve, keep it guarded so that the flesh goes through the hole in the throat and does not touch the throat but is placed according to its natural shape; then pull it gradually, leave it for some days, and treat with decayed onions until it heals; if the wound has pressed into the bone, dig it out; if there are pieces of bone, pull them all out as you can, and leave those that you cannot remove until the wound discharges and the discharge is dried and aligned; if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on it as I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, cure as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from spear or knife.   --> Of the spear or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a wound from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, check if air bubbles are coming out of the wound as the patient breathes: know then that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep but is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder immediately nor bind it for the blood will dissolve and return to the heart, and kill the patient; instead put on attractant ointment, and apply it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound for drainage and make the patient sleep on the wound 3 or 4 days, or more; no spasms nor bad tremor of heart nor any signs of breathing will come; and when you see good conditions, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat it (the wound) with cautery and other treatments while it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, open it up, then know that there is a fistula; treat it as necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 If the wound is from a sword or knife slice, and it is simple, or worse, on the surface, treat what is before (the affected area); if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, apply powder; and if it has gone into the bone, and pieces have been torn off, either clean the wound, and pull out the foreign objects if they are protruding; and if they are not protruding, let the wound fester, allow it to heal by itself; for other wounds on other limbs, the treatment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The dislocation of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The great, medium and small disembowelments are caused by a wound; from the large wound, the intestines occasionally protrude once, or the intestine's nerves, through which the insertion of foreign bodies occurs. The suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because it is more challenging to put the intestines back in, unless they are put back piece by piece; as the intestines inflate quickly, they return more easily, which makes medium-sized wounds preferable. Know that the disembowelment of the abdomen is according to four types: the two common suturing in the abdominal wound, and the suturing of other body wounds and the others specific are common in other wounds; however, they are more suitable for suturing the abdomen. I will explain each one individually.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines protrudes, it is easy to set, this is by one of the two methods: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are inflamed due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, heat it in any manner: moisten a sponge or wring out a damp cloth only, or you cook in hot squill and cyperus root and spike, and stretch the intestines until the inflammation is removed; and sometimes make this wine restraining, and it is boiled to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the inflammation separating, if you moisten the intestine with water or broth and herbs are cooked, because in this way the entrance is closed off almost entirely; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision at the instrument for cutting hemorrhoids; and the first cure is boiled to deflate, which we should not cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: if you split from within in the curve and do not widen, look at the shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines come out, put it back in its natural shape in its proper place, if you have the power to do so, for this is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is in the part beneath the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part beneath the belly, then lift the head and feet higher than the parts beneath, and likewise direct the opening of the belly to be higher in one of the two parts. And thus you should attend to what I say for large and minor wounds alike.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, use what you have at hand, then take a mildly skilled person who can cover the entire wound with his hand, and bring together the edges; and this is the usual method of suturing, and it is that you should take one or more needles, according to the size of the wound, then leave space from the edge of the wound, and stitch with a needle with a strong thread. And pierce the two layers of skin with the two layers of flesh, which is beneath the skin inside, so that you can pierce from this side, and bring together the two edges of the flesh threefold; then wrap a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring together the two edges of the wound again, and leave space, and stitch another. Then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease doing so according to how many needles you have, until the entire wound is stitched; and the needles should be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick, for thin needles pierce through all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they should be medium-sized; and do not push the needles too far away from the skin and flesh, so that they do not open the wound before it is sutured; and then close the heads of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put tents or cloths on the heads of the needles to hold them, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for it requires one needle or two for secondary sutures, and it is that you bring together the two layers of skin and the two layers of flesh with one needle and a strong medium-thread; and when you have pierced all four edges together, remove the needle to the part where you began, in the manner one cuts thread; and leave space between each suture the thickness of a small egg; this suturing is called home-made suturing, and I sewed a wound that a man had on his stomach, which was sliced by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and the intestines were well two palms wide, and the wound was within the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up for 15 days, healed, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 They judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicine; and I put on the wound old cotton twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle, and poke it from the outside to inside; when it has pierced the skin right through, place the end of the sinew or thread where you put the needle, and poke it from the inside to the outside again at that point; and the meaning of this stitching is that you sew as a tailor does with fur, leaving one side once, and taking it up again, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of sewing, as Galen calls it specifically, is performed in the following manner: take an awl or any other needle, and pierce only one side, leaving the two sides apart naturally; then turn the needle and pierce it from the outer part until the inner part, through both sides; then pierce both sides again from the outer part to the inner part, in the other two holes where the needle crosses each other; and this is the swaddling method of sewing and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens said this and it is witnessed by others, that the stomach should be sewn with two needles and thread in each; one needle should be inserted from one side and the other from the other, as those who sew leather do; and know that when there is a rupture within the stomach, the stitching is more difficult than on any other part of the stomach.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgments of the wound are as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you probe the fresh wound with all its blood, before the arrow has moved, you put back the intestine and the fat; then put powder healing char on it, and if the arrow has moved, put any ointment that is present, until the wound heals over; and sew up each end, and bind them with sifac and mirach; then treat the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you don't have medicines, immediately put old cotton on it, and stir it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 You do not need any other medicine for most simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound is communicating with the main members, then wet light linen in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the sore and under the saddle (bandage); and if there is pain or putrefaction in the belly, and this often occurs, then clisterize with black wine, especially when putrefaction comes to the intestines; and pierce it through, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The "youthful" intestine cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is due to the inflammation of veins that are present there, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the hernia jumps from the wound, put it back as the intestine is fresh; and if it is old and turned or black, you must cut away the black part where blood does not come, for there are veins and arteries; then take hold of what is between the ligament, and hang the two heads hanging from the part below the wound to straighten the extraction when the hernia falls, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 If the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, for I have seen that a man was pierced or his belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there was excrement and flatulence; I treated it according to what I knew, and did not cease to treat it until it was healed, and the hernias were sewn up.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I see it sutured, I feared that the patient had an issue in his stomach; and he had no ill there, but improved more favorably, ate, and drank; and any experimenters said that when a small wound is in the intestines, it should be tied up in this manner: take deep breaths with large gulps, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the breath has opened the mouth, place it between the lips so that it expands its mouth; and then strike the head, and keep it so that it cannot disconnect, then put another breath after in this manner until the wound is captured; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the head swells in the intestine and brings no harm to the patient, it can be tied with a thin thread made from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of the thread of intestine that is sharpened, then tie it to the head of the thread of linen, twist it, then put it on a needle and sew the intestine and tighten it as needed; and this method of stitching does not work except by faith and hope. If the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the larger intestines, there is no trick or healing, except for subtleness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or when it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it develops, is universally called "fistula", and likewise when it opens up and becomes hollow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And fistula is, according to the truth, a hard and white nodule, or there is no pain felt, and it is also hollow like the feather of a bird; sometimes clear bubbling, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times quite large; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is of no use unless due to one of the nine causes: namely, by the smallness of blood or body; or by its badness; or because there is hard flesh within, and above the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much bubbling; or the joint is dislocated, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in treatment; or the corruption is the nature of pestilence; or because the digestion is slow in the region, and late healing and wasting by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the medicines for cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must tell you the remedy for a fistula made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or the anus, or the intestine, or the bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine on the back, or any joints of the hands or feet; and such as affect the property of the main member, and similar locations.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all the fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the location I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you recognize it, take a tent made of fat or metal, if the fistula is straight, pierce it; and if the fistula is twisted, seek out a thin tent of reed, for the reeds bend with the twist; and if the fistula has been torn and you cannot find it with tents, cleanse it by one of the tears, for moisture moves from one tear to another and cleanses; then pierce it in a healthy manner to your ability, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and whether it is filled up, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when pressed by your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know the location where it is, and if it is distant from jointure, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the locations I have mentioned, then cut as I have told you, and remove the damaged tissue and rotten char inside; and then heal until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply rooted straight to the location, then cut deeply, as far as you can, then place moistened tents filled with medicine into the fistula, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluous matter left in the bottom; and then place healing ointments on clean char, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this means, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve does not bother you or your main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove all the corruption until it is completely removed, then treat with warm remedies until it heals; and if it does not heal, and turns bowed as before, know that you are not done yet: uncover it and clean it until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore its place; and if it heals in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If the corruption is too deep that you cannot reach it, know that you have no other remedy but to wait for nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone that can be extracted with pliers, extract it with an appropriate instrument; and if there are multiple bones, extract them all, not leaving any; and if moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, strike and force the moisture and heat, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove [the foreign body] within an hour, place something irritating pus on the wound and let it stay until the flesh is swollen around the bone, and then the bones will be more easily movable; and if it's a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, press down on the corruption only until all the blackness has been removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of the corruption that reaches the bone molecule, cover everything up to the corruption, and then heal it until it is healed; and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so you can take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 The young man was around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg due to something coming from within the body, which caused matter to come to the leg, and he had a large abscess that could not be drained; however, out of their folly, they operated on the abscess so much that the abscess opened, and they expelled much matter, and it became a fistula, and much pus flowed from his body and moisture from his corpse; and many tried to cure him for two years, but no skilled healer was found among them until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and that which flowed through the sores in great volume; and the young man's body became red, and he had a citrus-colored complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I inserted a tent (stitch) in one of the wounds, and then I searched all the wounds, and found that some were coming towards the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hurried then and dug in one of the wounds as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption was going towards the bone inside; what appeared to me as the rotten bone, I thought there was no other corruption except that which I left; and I began to heal the wound with salves for a long time, but could not close it; then I tried again, and discovered the bone again as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I tried to close the place; but I could not do so until I dug around a palm of the bone, and pulled out everything around it, then I healed it with salves; and it became healthy and closed quickly, but there was no need to continue the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for my fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Because of the blood evacuation, it often became healthy entirely, and grew in the bone a hard cyst, and was of good condition and had no harm or contrary effect in any way, neither at its side nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated as follows: take a thread, and fasten it to the open end of the bone, and command someone to pull it up; then place another thicker thread over the cyst that is above the bone, and tie it so that you draw the corrupted cyst down, exposing the healthy cyst where you wish it to be, so that it does not hurt the healthy cyst; then place charcoal or a plaster under the bone to cover the corrupted cyst; and it must be done as much as can be seen and felt, and again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, uncover all the flesh; then put fire beneath, and then soak from one side to another the corrupted area, and let the iron be as long as the length of the corrupted area as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, strike the corrupted joint, and hold the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other instrument but to cover it; and if the corruption is at the end of the hand or foot, it is a difficult matter, but still you must investigate the corruption, how it opens; and clean it in all the ways that you can, but ensure that the vein or nerve do not oppose you; and know that the instruments for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bone and the appearance of the opening, and its thickness and subtlety, and its size and smallness, and hardness; and because of this, it is necessary to equip oneself with an instrument suitable for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the diseases; and choose the instrument that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	the fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head may be corroded either from within or from without; and when you have administered that corrosive medicine for its cure with medicines, and it does not help, then you must cover the affected limb up to where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient may escape death or a more severe illness due to the fault of the limb; and the signs are that the limbs become black, as if they were burned by fire, and afterward becomes darker; the corruption then spreads from limb to limb and takes over the whole body; hasten to cover [the area]; and if it is caused by the sting of any venomous creatures like sea scorpion or viper and similar, cover the head of the affected area, and do not give it room to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it comes up to the wrist, strike at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, strike at the edge; and if it passes the edge, it is death, and no remedy is of use except for the amount of its virtue; and thus do as when the corruption comes or pierces: if it comes at the first joint, then strike after the other joint; and if it comes or pierces, then strike all the way; and if it moves in the leg, then strike at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy except for letting the patient die; and the method of striking or healing the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one servant one chain below, and another servant the other chain above, and you separate the flesh which is between the two chains with a spatula wide enough so that the bone is exposed; then strike or heal, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the heated iron does not touch the healthy part, and brings the patient another injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	1. And if bleeding comes when you are working, then cauterize the place immediately, or apply some restraining powders; return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb with a sturdy rope and cure it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my time: he had a blackness that looked like burnt by fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot, consuming all of it; and when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly covered the foot, and it healed; and for a long time afterward the corrosion returned to his hand or foot, and came to me, and I gave him healing remedies after the body's purification, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he asked me to amputate his hand, and I did not wish, as I had hope of healing it; and I feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die, for the man's vitality was weak; and he lost all hope, and returned to his earth, and quickly covered his hand, and it healed; and I have never heard of such a thing except as a caution, in case it is needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes an abscess occurs in a charnut (arm) and remains for such a long time that it forms a large swelling; then it ruptures and perforates, and the arm remains visible, like a servant's; and the skin that is over it is as thin as linen fabric torn, and does not reach the bone or the nerve. Such an illness is called "sain", but if it extends to the bone fully, it is called "fistule"; and you should cut all the affected skin around it, and even when it is thin, like linen; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if the skin hardens and corruption is not complete, and the skin is thickened with pus, cure it with a clysterium (enema) in this way: look to see if the breasts are large and the nipples that are in them smell foul, then clysterize with an Egyptian medicine which is made as follows: take asafetida, oil, and pitch, equally, and cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take as much as necessary for your use, and make it into water and honey, and clysterize the breast, and press out the pus; leave the medicine there for two hours, then release it by straining; do this many times, until the breast is healed and the pus is gone; and at no time is a clysterism of water from ashes used, unless this medicine is not present, and you use vinegar ash instead, and pour water over it, then strain, and clysterize until you know that the breast is well healed; and if the patient cannot endure this, or the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then clysterize with water and honey or mead, for the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the blood flow; and when you have done this, and have confidence that the breast is well cleansed, then clysterize with what causes pus to grow in it, and take wormwood oil and vinegar; or clysterize with various medicines and ointments, of which I have told their properties or treatments; and if the opening of the nipple is small, and the clyster's nozzle cannot enter, then enlarge it slightly with a knife, and apply an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then bind it up and leave only enough room for the clyster to enter, and if the nipple that smells foul is above, then press down or lower the nipple.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the intestine is full, do not allow any gas to enter it; and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus as you wish, arrange it in such a way that the intestine moves to its lowest position, because when the intestine is fully expanded, do not allow any gas to enter it and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus as you wish, arrange it in this manner: let the intestine move gently downward, and leave nothing of the intestine; take consolidating medicines to apply on the wound, and place a linen cloth over the entire wound; then press forcefully towards the opening of the wound, closer to the navel, which is wider than the first one, because it is immediately sealed with another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it on the opening of the wound to align the intestine, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days; the cloth placed on the opening of the wound should be frequently removed to release the intestine, and you should know if it is venom or pus or too much, or indigestible; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in this manner and you see the nature that arises on the opening of the wound, know that the intestines have burst open, and move towards healing; then unbind it in the morning, or the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	If the breasts are swollen and do not improve after several days, know that they will not swell further.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisonous worms crawl for a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For those who suffer from pus in their wounds and for those who do the opposite; and if one eats indigestible food for many days, know that the breast will not heal; and if the breast does not heal and swells, use drying medicines with a dry substance and wet virtue, such as mustard, for there is great part of vitriol, which is the last medicine; take mustard, and make it with rose oil, and equal old wine in substance; then heat and apply; and do the same with cooked mustard when mustard is not present, or you take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them, powder over the honey when it is on the fire; and then spread it on the cloth and place it on the breast, and sometimes administer long aristolochia root and celestial root, which is also like flour and centory; and use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make into powder, and put on the honey as said above, and use it. And if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this remedy, know that corruption has penetrated fully, and made an impression in the bone or hard members or tendons; if the breast is cured, use the fistula cure as said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess at the nailbed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Panarice is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or it may arise in other places; and when it is swollen, and no care is taken, if it bursts open, it runs and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly it will corrode completely; and the corruption goes to the bone, until there is a foul-smelling pain, and the joints of the finger or toe are wide, and the color is yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the previous section and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail, followed by cauterizing the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail pushes into the flesh and starts to point, and the blood blisters, you must place the heat under the nail so that it doesn't push the flesh, but press on it gently and lightly. Then apply hot and corrosive medicines on top of it to burn everything away; afterward, heal it with ointments until it heals completely.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 If the corrosion is in the bone, strike it and draw out pus because as much as the bone gets corrupted, it cannot heal. And if you see that the bone is corroding, strike it with a sharp spoon as previously mentioned, then heal it until it heals completely; and if it is wounded and hurts intensely, you must disinfect it first. Then cut the nail with a sharp spatula from one side, making sure that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail because the patient would feel too much pain. And if this happens, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deaf man's hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The patient must cauterise who is born with a growth in some people's hands by chance, which is entirely flesh, and sometimes it has bone, and occasionally it has nail; and one of these never grows from the joint root or the growth emerges from any of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one born in any finger does not grow, and the one born at the joint of a finger may grow; the size of the fleshy one is light, in this way: cut it off at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	If one is born at the root of the join, he is difficult to cure; keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one born or should be in the little finger, it is necessary that you cut round the flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same sores that come at the joints come together by birth, or by injury of a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If it is necessary for you to sew that wound, let it heal according to its natural shapes; then place between two tents or dampened cloths in oil, so that they do not stick together; or put between two thin pieces of wood until the wounds are healed, as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	In the same way, if any of his hands comes with the palm, then strike that joint as necessary.
des vils	 of peasants
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 The veins are large swollen ones filled with melancholic fluids that come in many members of the body, and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must sometimes administer purge of bile, and then let it flow from the basilica (biliary duct).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The iron cure is according to two methods: one is to sew it and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you tie off the vein and let all the blood flow out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The thigh is performed in this manner: First, the leg is heated with strong hot water until the flesh becomes tender, then hold the patient's leg above the knee up to the part below the thigh; then cut the vein in I, II or III, of a large size, then separate and draw out black blood to your hand from one end to the other, as much blood as the disease can withstand; and then tie it, and commands him to bind himself with meat that stimulates black colic; and start the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, which benefits the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The incision is performed in this manner: place the patient's leg, if there is much hair, then immerse it in water or bathe it, and heat the leg with warm water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have water, heat it over fire, and then make a long incision towards the thigh at the top of the knee or below at the ankle; then peel the skin along the incision, and scrape the vein from both sides until it appears when felt; and you see red and black, and when it appears under the skin, it resembles a white cord; then push the fat down, until the vein is raised above the skin, and then make a light cut at the incision, then make another incision 3 inches further away; then peel the skin over the vein until it appears again, then draw out the blood as before, and make another cut, as you did previously; then make another incision, or more if necessary, then draw out, and make a cut at the end of the thigh, then pull and drain until it is completely drained, then press; and if you cannot draw it and lift it, insert a thick double threaded needle into it, tie and draw, and push it under the fat, and turn your hand from one side to another, until it comes out; and be careful not to cut, because if it cuts, you cannot draw or lift it, and it is harmful to the patient; and when you have treated it all, place linen dampened in wine and oil on the wound site; and care for it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is contracted, twisted and rolled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, you must cut it forcefully, but do not cover it; drag it as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to strike the face should be curved and not sharp, striking the vein; it is large in curvature, because if it were thin, it would pierce the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	 of the common vein (civil vein)
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is inserted in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry soil without moisture; and by chance it may appear elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes from below the skin, as it comes within the body serpents and worms, inserting between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very large inflammation comes in the leg, then the limbs change and the vein begins to burst out like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the thigh is opened, you must roll around a piece of plank from one and a half to two feet long, and sew it, leaving the plank next to the leg, and each time when it pours out at the opening, you roll it around the plank and sew; and if it is too long, cut a part of it, roll the remaining part, and do not cover its root, until it all bursts out; for if you cover it, it returns into the flesh, causing an abscess and pus or swelling at the limb, and a bad disease. Therefore, it must be treated slowly to the groin, and nothing remains in the body; and this vein sometimes when it is treated can be seven or ten fingers long, or even more, and once a man came to me, whose vein burst out ten fingers long, and when you press it, you bring out pus or blood, and pierce it to its bottom, so that everything comes out; empty the matter inside, and introduce medicines against pus for several days to the limb, then cure it as with an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes the vein opens on its own, especially when it is opened at the joint of the foot or hand, causing great loss and hemorrhage; treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh and moves throughout the body expanding and contracting, causing pain in one member after another until it bites through the skin or bursts; and it is infested with corruption of some humors, as snakes and serpents and roundworms and tapeworms or intestinal parasites; and there is doubt about its malice, for when it moves through the body and rises to the head, it may reach the eye and enter, and destroy the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it to cure and drain, one cannot force it except when it goes: therefore, you must lie the limb above and below with a strong rope tightly tied, then strike upon it and draw out, and if its opening is full in the flesh and you do not open it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest damage that it does is that it causes oil to flow, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, hold a clamp underneath it in the shape of a horseshoe, then strike upon it and draw out; and the patient must use remedies for purification of the body with soluble medicines for bad humors to pass, and avoid rich foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and it is a pain that comes in certain limbs, and moves from one limb to another; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was summoned to a sick woman, and I saw her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and afterwards, I saw it rise like a worm toward the shoulder, faster than anything, as living silver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain separated from that place and pierced the shoulder, and shortly after ran throughout the body, until she came into the other arm; then she told me that it repeatedly returned around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly surprised how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this kind of disease in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 I would have wanted many that they moved the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed, and because of this, such constricted windiness appeared; and it does not apply according to this reason to those who are fat or have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if she opens as we have said, then close it quickly both inside and outside, and then press on top so that such constricted windiness leaves the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes, cure it with those who drive out windiness, such as fetid pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	 Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows or needles come in different types, depending on their shapes and the parts of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The varieties of them are such that there are those with large points and small, smooth or grooved, solid or barbed; and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have fragments; and when it strikes any member, it strikes in several ways: either in the main member, which pierces like the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it strikes any location in these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you afterwards indicates: if you wish to extract this arrow, for many deaths follow in various dispositions; and when this ill sign does not indicate, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, pull it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.
