And the signs of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces the skull, and the swelling that is on the brain, are scotomia (loss of vision), sode (numbness or weakness in the limbs), esvertin (seizures), and roujor (reddening) among the eyes, inflammation and reddening of tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, vomiting of bile; and possibly without swelling from the nose, or ears; and possibly loss of speech and voice; and from the wound swells moist white matter resembling pus, and also as does bruise of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, beware of treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The sign of the arrow when it strikes or pierces is that it is near the left breast, and feels like it has been driven into something hard, not empty; and by chance the arrow may become silent like a pulse, and brings cold blood, and cold sweat, and faintness: know for certain that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that pierces the body is when a scab does not rise from the wound and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, breathes heavily and seeks warm air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow falls on the bed of the sick person, it has pierced the sides; and he spits a large amount of saliva and feels great pain and breathes heavily; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead or stomach falls out by chance, anything from the undigested flesh may jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrowhead or abdomen falls out and something from the intestinal tract jumps out, there is no hope in the treatment nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrowhead falls into the bladder and urine jumps out and spills, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the hand, arm, neck, shoulder, backbone, waist, hips, legs, and those similar, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, for this reason you should do something else.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 If an arrow falls or pierces in the root of a man's neck, I pulled it out from another side beneath the ear fat, and it healed without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And pulled out a arrow that had fallen in the fat of the oil beneath the paper beneath, and the arrow was bent, and could not be straightened except for the tip towards the body, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, to all the light iron ears; the man healed, and no ill accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And take an arrow out of the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I was the barber, and I sharpened it so much that I pulled it out, and the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And draw out an arrow from a man who was wounded or stabbed in the chest, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrowhead, looped it, and pulled it out without any ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 If you want to remove an arrow from a man who fell on his back and the wound was sutured over it, let it remain inside him for a while; if it does not cause a natural change in his condition or cause any harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And if another man falls an arrow in his face, and the wound is sewn up; and he endures thus without suffering great pain; and many other such things happen.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And a spear hit the king of princes, who fell in the snow, and was leaning slightly to the right side; and the spear was completely embedded. I was called to treat him three days after it happened.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I pierced it with a fine needle and felt nothing; yet he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the tip of the spear. I applied an absorptive and digestive plaster to the place, because the flesh did not swell; and the handle of the spear appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I kept the plaster for many days, and healed the wound straight, and the patient stayed like that for a long time, until he felt the arrow within his stomach; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I placed a corrosive medicine on the wound for many days until it was opened, and then I tried, and felt the head of the arrow protruding from its place; then I inserted in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared clearly visible to me; and he lived beyond four months, and then the wound that I sewed with the pliers broke open again on one side and the other, and could not heal; therefore, I did not stop refining and devising ways to extract it, until I made the pliers well according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, as I drew it out and returned the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the physicians judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored; I then restore it, and the wound is healed, and the patient is completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows; put your care upon this that I am not saying everything, for the books cannot fully grasp it; but wise masters compare well little things, and upon what is present and lacking, they find nine works and nine instruments in the art's removal of strange things that happen in it.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not enter the limb where they are thrust except in two ways: either through the side or through the place from which they come out; and the one that jumps out where it enters is an arrow piercing through flesh, and sometimes jumps out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, leave it until the char is able to be put around [it], and align the issue; and likewise, if it has been driven into the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it for some days, move it every day; then it will jump, and if it does not jump, pierce all around with a very sharp instrument until the area around is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is driven into the head of the bone and goes up to one of the brain ventricles, or any of the accidents I have mentioned above happen to the patient: do not pull it out immediately, but leave it until it aligns after some days, because if the arrow reaches such a point, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrowhead is not embedded beyond the bone but has not been extracted, and the patient suffers for some days with bad condition, try to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply inserted and cannot come out, then administer tourniquets around it, as I told you before; then heal the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is lodged within the body and cannot be seen, press it with all your might; if you feel it, extract it with any suitable instrument; if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, widen the wound as much as possible; extract the arrow and break off the ears (shaft extensions) if it has them, remove the flesh that is embedded in its tips as much as you can, then bend or break the shaft ears until you can draw it out; be careful not to break the arrow so as to pull it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, pull down the leg to the joints, then draw, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood opposes it (the cautery), bring to mind what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of incising a nerve or vein, and use an instrument as you can draw out the arrow safely, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do it, place him as the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from elsewhere and opens something of it or the skin is swollen in one place where it can be seen or felt: cut then above, as far as the pliers can grasp, and then pull it out; if it jumps away now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it [the dislocation] is held within the bone, you should turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot be extracted, leave it for a while, and then continue the extraction until it is fully emerged; and if it is from an arrowhead, push it all in; and if it has fallen out, you should use tweezers to administer grip, so that the point of the arrowhead enters the grip of the tweezers; and then push further, and if the arrowhead is gripped, push the tweezers in with the pointed end entering, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 If the arrowhead is touching [the body], it is necessary to cut around the affected area where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If the arrowhead falls into the groin or belly or bladder or side and it is near and you can cover it, then do so; but be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then remove it, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and care for it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tweezers used to remove arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The form of the buttock hair is similar to the feathers of a bird, for pushing the point of an arrowhead, as shown here: [no further English text provided]
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tweezers for pushing and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Incisions of the common body cavities
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 Of the veins from which one recovers are thirty-one, of which the first sixteen are: two glands located behind the ears, which are called the "dou herbech"; and the two arteries in the temples; and the two veins that are in the eyesockets, called "aspires"; and the vein on the forehead; and the vein at the top of the nose; and the two neck veins; and the two veins in the upper lips above the mouth, these veins are called "augeherich"; and the two veins under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins commonly cleansed are five in each arm: one is called the cephalic, located on the left side of the chest and the common people call it "arm vein"; the median is called "fistula", composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; the basilic is either on the right side of the chest and the common people call it "ventricle vein", located above the elbow and the one that is opened clearly near the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the ulnar vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, which has two rains; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one located under the wrist of the left side of the chest, and the second saphenous vein that is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nese", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The ancient cathartics aid the swellings that are behind the ears and migraines; they help them move. The qualities of the cathartic, as I tell you, are that you seize the patient's head, and rub the place where the swellings or veins are with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw, so that the two swellings appear behind the ears in the two dependent places on the head; when you feel the pulse under your hand, push; then take the lancet, and thrust it through the swelling right up to the bone, then grip all the swelling with your whole hand and pierce the skin and the swelling well two times through, and make blood come out until you see; then bind and hold it until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The following of the second artery that are in the temples is useful for migraines, old sores, and frequent headaches; and the qualities of the healer are as I say: and it is that the patient lowers his neck, until the two veins appear openly; and you feel a pulse beneath your thumb, then press it; next lift the skin on the vein towards the top of your thumb, and push the lancet into it; lift the vein up, and pierce, as you have done in the other veins, and draw off the blood according to your need; then release the patient, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; next form a knot, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about its compression and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The opening of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein in ancient facial diseases, and it has migrated and reddened; and its qualities are such that the patient twists his neck while straining, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let blood come out according to the amount you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein when it is healthy and never use a large flame for work.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	In addition, the flames should not be too sharp; and obliquely, because the bone is near, and by chance the flames may break when they are fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The opening of the two veins that are in the eyes helps with pain, tension, reddening, swelling in the eye, and facial diseases; and the qualities of their opening are such that the patient twists his neck while pulling a cord, as mentioned before; then release it, and make the incision across the flame, a little long and wide, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the fire is thin, perhaps it may break; then correct the blood flow, as much as you need, and then cover it with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The vein from the neck is useful for ague, scrod disease and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that occurs in the face and especially when it is old. The qualities of the vein are that the patient compresses his neck, then compresses his neck with your left hand, takes subtle long flame, and thrusts it between the two nostrils because the vein does not open easily elsewhere, and the wound will begin to heal; do not go too deep, and make a wound according to necessity, then let it rest for a night as it is quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The straining of the two tendons aids in the stretching of the ankle, and at the beginning of swelling, and in many diseases, and in inflammation, and in rotting, and in sores, and in abscesses; and the quality of the strain is that the patient stretches his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and the master being above the patient's head, and the patient lying on the chair, then strains the vein along its length a little widely, then draws blood gently or as much as needed; then he does the same in the other vein, then releases the ligament, and holds the veins moderately so that the patient does not strain; and leaves it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the livestock health
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment of mouth boils also helps with cold in the mouth and corruption of the gums, and cuts and sores around the mouth.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of health are to make the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the ear, and look at the two veins, one on the right ear and the other on the left, and they are recognized by the fact that they are dark, and by the fact that around them there are small dark veins: thus grab one and the other, and if you do not know which one it is, or if you doubt, grasp the larger of each side, and similarly for the two veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the livestock health below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The livestock health beneath the tongue aids after the cephalic health examination, and it is in the tightening of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the healer are that the patient must sit between your hands before the sun, and lick the tongue, and look below on each side for a dark vein: grasp one and the other, but do not go too deep because below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins that are usually opened for healing are opened according to two methods: either by pricking all the way with a wide iron, or with subtle olive oil as you cut through, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 It is necessary to open wide and flat veins that contain thick blood and are troubled, and this is the form of the olive oil fire.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointedly subtle, and is for healing subtle veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with the diseases that are under the throat, and neck, and chest, and abdomen; and it is necessary for the patient to be healed thoroughly, and to empty the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if it strikes the artery and bleeding comes out, it should be stopped, as I have said; but do not prick with fire, but cut like a surgeon's lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basilica does not open clearly, you must force it to open and change another one or look for any opening in it from the arm; it will open clearly; then prick with a surgeon's lancet like we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you want to locate the place of the opening, then you must also force the arm and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with a cross, tie the arm, and prick the vein with a surgeon's lancet; beware that you do not pierce the artery when you see it swell up, for it is the artery; so avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it rise high as a child's urine and the limb is red and tender, know that it is not from an artery: therefore hurry up, place your finger on it for a long time, then cut off your finger when it becomes insensate, which often happens; if it's an arm, leave it like that, and don't let the patient move it; and be afraid, and don't let it move until it gets better.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the limb is not bleeding and it pains you, and there is no medicine present, then cut open the artery if it opens, because the head of the limb will retreat; stop the bleeding from the limb.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a piece of willow bark, cut it and take one half and hold it on top until the next day; if it becomes insensate, that's good; if not, heal it as we have said with powders that stop blood; and stopping the bleeding is not to be delayed due to the slightness of the wound or the tightness of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from both the head above and the body below, as it is composed of the basilica and cephalica, as we have said; and the surgeon should pierce it for the nerve that is below, and if he pierces too deeply and finds the nerve, it inflates and the limb becomes numb or painful, and there is a risk that it will not heal; and this nerve opens frequently, and if it does not open in any human being due to its subtlety, you must use an instrument to cleanse it; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The vein in the head also helps to drain blood from the eyes and assists in healing them; and it should be pierced with olive oil or myrtle fire, as this is the safest of all veins, as there is no nerve or artery below it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Therefore, it is necessary to seek out the lighter joint, and not to worry if it needs to be done for the first time, and you can start over; and sometimes the joint swells in some people, but do not worry for the first time, but do nothing.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of urine is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing that you should know about bloodletting is that it is not done except to maintain health and to avoid future diseases; and bloodletting should be performed in one of the three veins: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilic; and bloodletting should be done at the beginning of spring or autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; and bloodletting should be done on the first day or third day, three hours after or two days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The salve for illnesses does not have a set hour determined, but it is administered when needed, either day or night, at all hours and in every time; and it should not be applied to children until they are 14 years old, nor to women during pregnancy until the fourth month, up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Old people over sixty years old should not be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 When anyone wishes to be healed, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that their intestines are cleansed with a light clyster, if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not expel the superfluous waste into the principal members; nor should it be treated those who are overly salty from foods, or drunk, as long as they remain drunk; nor those who are dropsical; and if one wishes to heal after a colic attack, vomiting, and abdominal distention, and multiple diarrhea in women, and too much labor, watchfulness, and fasting, and those who exhaust themselves with the power of their arm or their body; then refine the humors, if they are fat, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the ability to do so; then immerse in a bath, unless something prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and heal from the vein on the side opposite the third, as we have said; and take care of that day to abstain from work, pain, luxury, and similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the healer stand above the one being healed, and rub the arm two or three times, then gently pull the ligament upwards, for when it is too tight or narrow, it cannot heal without; then rub the area around the wound with your hands until the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the healer's fingers with a little old oil, then place his palm of his left hand on the vein below the area to be healed, so that the vein does not fail or escape from being struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 There are veins that flee like cords in a sieve, and some are filled with ventosity, so that when you put on the flame, it retreats from the flame and cannot open the vein, thus is one of these; if the vein swells, the wound is too narrow, for this reason the sewer should be advised in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If it opens the first time, that's fine; but if not, restart from the same place or shortly thereafter, unless the limb is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 If the limb swells and the patient fears, let him wait a day or two, do not tie the arm: perhaps abscesses will come out; do not enter in the bath, then resume the sewer if he wishes; and if the opening is small, or the wound is shallow and you doubt that it is not flowing much blood as you see, be brave with that opening itself directly to all the flame; and open it a little hastily, so that the limb does not swell; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the joint swollen, do not start the bleeding, but put a little bit of oil on it, as it will alleviate the body from blood, and the oil will be coagulated in this place; and administer the oil in every bleeding that you perform on veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same does triacle and bowe when placed on the joint; if it is too thick, it becomes more subtle.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 If a large abscess occurs, which often happens when the incision of the vein is small, hurry and put on the joint a sponge wet with vinegar and warm linen, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood flow from the vein, and if it remains in the place after several days without any blackness or greenness, it does not matter; and if you see, put anything of aloes or myrrh on it, grounded with a pestle and mortar, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often abscess and appearance appear at the healing of the basilica: place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to pressure from the hand, then that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything above what has been said, because by chance without the artery; but let it be one plug of dry material to harden the place, then cure it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out blood from each person according to the quantity of its strength and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for those who are swollen and burst, and have need of bloodletting, to make a larger incision; and for the weak ones, do the opposite, and it is necessary to leach pus frequently, and one must leach it by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of leaching is safe from disruption of blood and compression of nerves, and it is worth more than leaching deeply rather than widely.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 For the one whose body needs leeching, it is necessary to give moistened bread in the form of pomegranates; if he is feverish, let him bleed three or four times. And for those of cold complexion, let them fast before the leeching with moistened bread in a sweet syrup, or sweet syrup made from honey and aromatic spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if the wound is bleeding profusely after dislocation, it is necessary that you apply a paste of charcoal and sweet-smelling subtle syrup, and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for blood evacuation.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to dislocate someone's arm and then relocate it at another time, when it has been weakened by much bleeding, it should be done little by little, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to dislocate someone's arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong heart, should wait 9 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another part, should be bled on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood inside the body which is already boiling and causing fever; it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, open the wound completely until it bleeds through the palm of the hand; then you must follow all the conditions for bleeding, place your hand on top of the pulses when it stops bleeding to prevent death from coming in its place, which happens often when the blood-letters are negligent; and it is not necessary to release the arm and draw blood a second time if the wound is closed again, press firmly instead; nor should you stretch the arm forcefully if it is curved, but let it be until it bleeds a second time; or prick the tip of the flame until the congealed blood exits from the vein, and place a piece of fresh linen on top, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if a vein has burst, let it be and do not compress it until the abscess is pacified.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If it requires drawing blood a second time, draw it from the same place, or another vein, or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is safer to use instead of the one in the neck because it is composed of different vessels.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of the bleeding is that the patient pushes his hand into hot water until the flesh becomes red; then it should be tied moderately, so that the vein appears well; then press the hand with a probe, not too wide or too long; and let it be pierced widely, and let the vein be pricked close to the joint of the hand, and if one cannot extract it, put the hand back into hot water and let the blood flow out in the water until you have enough; and if it is winter, do not hit the hand with hot water again, for it puts more winter there than in summer; and the vein of this kind is safer than all other veins, as there are no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The incision of the palm of the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases, and this is how it's done: strain the hand, and press it with hot sharp, until the vein is evacuated, if you can see it; and if it is transverse, and you cover it entirely, let nothing bother it; and don't push too deep, because nerves are all exposed beneath skin, then replace the hand in hot water, provided that the wound isn't frozen, and it cannot be pulled out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as needed, put oil and linen over the wound to heal quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purification of the hand on the left side is beneficial for the disease of paralysis, and it should be done in the same way as I told you concerning the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The incision of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all the diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of phlegm, and disease of the kidneys, and the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the qualities of its health are such that the patient should put their foot in hot water and rub on the vein until it perishes, and tie above the joint of the foot; and when the vein is at the ankle, and over the foot it goes a great distance; therefore open wider the vein or at the ankle, which is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you lay it on the leg below, watch out for nerves that are beneath it, and lay it through just as in cutting; let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the leg cannot be extracted, place it in the water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if it is necessary to open the vein for the first time, then start again a little above because salt is present there; do not doubt of the nerve, as we have said, and proceed similarly with the opening of the equal foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The salted area of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its blister is worth the pain of the heel when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the qualities of its health are that the patient immerses themselves or wrings above the ankle four times while twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then you should let it bleed in all ways that you can, and across; it is more effective to cover it because the salve is dry and it responds well to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't set it right, no medicine will help the man who has a wound or fracture in the back, and towards the small of his back, beware of nerves; do as much as you can to stop the bleeding, then untie the ligament, put cotton on it and press; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of blistering sores
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters (of cupping) are made from horns or goat's horn, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by bleeding and drawing blood, or without bleeding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this blistering, which is like wounding, is of two kinds: either all fire, or with heat; and the blistering caused by wounding and bloodletting is done in 14 places in the body, from which one is entirely in the head; and the others are at the neck; and two on the chests of the neck; and one under the chin; and one in the shoulders; and one in the elbows; and one in the wrists; and one in the knees; and one in the ankles; and one in the heels; and this blistering does not treat blood, unless it is small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and for that reason, it should not be applied at all, neither with hot fire nor without heat, in any disease that comes from swelling, until all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if due to necessity or habit, fumigation is required for the sick, we will administer it each hour at the beginning of the month or at its end; and during and in every time, as there are some who, when they need to be fumigated, have a heavy head; and some who find fullness and redness in their face, neck, and throat; and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue swells and bleeds; and there are those who think, see bloody stools and vomit and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	When we see these signs and especially when it is in the month [of the disease], we order to bleed after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The smoke of the mouth helps alleviate headache ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this fumigation is in place of cranial sweating, and it should not be used by those with a cold complexion or who have diarrhea, as it does great harm to them; and for that reason, neither watchmen nor those with colds or headaches should use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become obtuse, and for this reason, the blister should be placed a little lower due to the risk of becoming obtuse.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventosation in the neck is located near the sinus of the head and the basilica, which makes it effective for the narrowing of the windpipe, splitting of the channel of the throat, choking, and filling; however, it should not be pushed too hard because if it holds too firmly, it may cause obstruction or asphyxia or heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosation to the chest in the neck is beneficial for headaches, earache and migraines, strangulation, pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is located near the sinus of the basilica; you should instruct the patient to press gently with their hand when doing it, not to touch the artery, and not to cause excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilations under the chin are good for mouth disease and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it should be in the positions of the two cheeks.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations of the shoulders are good for disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The ventosations of the sides is as much as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; instruct the lord not to press too deeply, for the flesh is bare and knows beneath it nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The boil on the buttock is effective for treating hemorrhoids at their base and diseases underneath, and it should be large and made of lard, as it needs to be well-drawn; and if it were subtle, it would break; and in that case, it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The boils on the legs open widely because they draw blood from the whole body, and they are effective for treating old pains in the joints, such as those of the knees and ankles, and they remove the flower; and they are located between the shins and the knees, and the ankles, and although they weaken the body after long use, they bring down pus in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the boil is that you put it first and apply it promptly, press it evenly, and continue this action until you see the place turning red and swelling, and opening the redness of blood; then wait and put the boils back, taking care in the disposition of the body, as there are those with soft skin and clear pores: it is necessary to cut only once, and it is necessary to make wide and deep wounds, and a little superficially.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the limb is thick, it should be cut twice: the first time to make a path for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the limb is very thick, it should be cut three times; and when we want to draw out the thin blood, we only need to prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want much blood, let us often encourage it; and if the skin is thick, press deeply, and let the wound be such that the veins are pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, to anoint the lees of the ventosations with stimulating and dissolving oil: if in summer, oil of violets, or sweet almond oil, or seed oil of cucumber; and if in winter, oil of parsley, or lily, or camomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluidity is large and cold, take amat oil, or balm of Gilead oil, or anise oil, and others like it.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one whom you are treating has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil should be applied; instead, it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or water of morello cherries, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or some similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And one who has much moisture, if he rises from bed, should do so with asafetida or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or water of blood, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or some similar; and it is not necessary to ventosate before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and he should not sleep after the ventosation, and it is necessary that he urinate, when he needs to be ventosed and when he has been ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And keep in mind that one who heals is coleric, and the patient lacks moisture and is inflamed too much; then it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green apples, endives, lettuces for drink, and similar items; eat little meat, beef liver, and moist food.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And one who has a cold complexion, let him take honey syrup, fragrant mild wine that is neither old nor new, and eat pepper, and fish, and small birds and sparrows; on the day he will vomit, he should drink more than eat; it is also necessary to give certain men sometimes three grains of triacet or musk before or after vomiting, to strengthen the main organs; and let the patient be thin, but not those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The following harrowing are the blisters placed to wound are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, gout, stomach and belly, loins and hips, for these members cannot bear being wounded elsewhere; they are applied only to draw blood from one member to another, as we do with breasts when a woman is lactating; to remove viscosity from the affected member, as we apply blisters on the stomach and belly to reduce the swelling; and to alleviate pain, when there is abscess or stone, it draws the abscess by its attractive power accidentally, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus it functions when applied on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these blisters are administered empty for sucking only; sometimes they are administered with fire, and at other times filled with cold water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in this manner a blister is filled with hot moist water or hot water containing boiled herbs such as comfrey.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the blister to be treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers and a half width and a palm-length long, and have a small notch on the side near the middle, as for pushing an awl, and be made of ivory in front so as not to prick the patient when placed on the member; and there should be a rod of a cubit in length through the middle of ivory or metal, to hold a splint in place, and they should be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the swellings of children are other than those of adults, and thin ones than fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this splint should be placed thus on the member: take a band of wax or linen and place it inside the notch in the splint so that the light is at the bottom of the splint to prevent it from burning the patient; then place the splint on the member, with the fingers over the notch as we have said, so that when one looks, if steam comes out, remove the splint; and take the linen again as before, and renew it frequently, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the bladder (ventouse), which is administered in pleurisy disease, it has no worm nor puncture, and it should not be done unless when it is full of fluid, and it should only be placed on the member; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Sansues (bladders) should not be administered in small areas such as lips and gums, as well as other similar places; and in the bare skin, such as fingers or eyes, and other similar places; and the quality of the practitioner is that when you find bladders in clear, sweet, net fluids without pus, you should take them; place them in a container with sweet fluid, until they become familiar and have nothing inside; then let it be strained from vein and bladder, then rub the member till it becomes red, and put the bladders on top of it; when they become full and warm, if it is possible to apply bladder there, do so, because this is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If it is not so, raise the shoulder blade slightly, then deeply and very well, and press; and if the shoulders are too close to each other after the body, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, place it over, until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling multiplies, place broken vitriol or alum, or similar things over it until it subsides; or you put half of peeled fennel seeds on the shoulder, and leave them until they adhere to the shoulder, it will now subside; and if you need more help, take other swellings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 If the swellings do not want to take, rub the shoulder with fresh blood, or you prick it with a needle until the swelling comes out, and then place them over, and as soon as they feel the blood, they adhere; when you see that they drip, sprinkle some powder of aloe and silk or ash on top, they will now cease.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures (breaks)
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with setting fractures and dislocations.
