Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Inform, dear son, that the foolish one should abandon this chapter, for they will never see any of the ancient books nor read letters from them; and because of this, the science is strange in our land, for I have never found it good; and I do not know anything about it except through the science of the ancient books, which I have studied extensively and have treated, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are brought forth, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we explain the summary of this book's content and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 When any fracture or dislocation or twisting or sprain occurs to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from both sides, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of body, old age, or infancy; or if the time is not very warm, or too cold; and give them cold broths, namely cold meats, eye-salve and lamb's wool, and do not drink wine, nor consume fatty foods, nor fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about abscess heat or the spreading of matter to the member; then the patient returns to their first government as they had used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed on foods that cause thick stools, or have viscosity like cooked barley in water and peas, and beef, and pork, and veal, and mutton, and eggs, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this thick stool, the healing of the fracture is quicker.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones in the elderly and weak cannot be well regained or repaired according to their nature due to the relaxation of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, as bones of small children; but do not worry, set on top of the broken bone the large tendons that bind and join the member together, as much as possible, so it heals as it was before; and do not touch it at all, and therefore feed it with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head (skull) is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture which goes towards the elbow, and another in sharpening, like the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each has its device and tool in restoration, according to what memory comes in its place; and it is known that the bone breakage occurs when the joint is twisted, and opened wide by displacement, and then compressed with the hand; and when there is no distortion nor the patient feels great pain, there is no fracture; but it can have distortion or fissure, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand at all, but place medicine on it that comes afterwards, and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the breaks which go towards the elbow, and are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary to set them equally aligned now, so that abscesses do not grow there; and if abscesses grow there, leave it for some day until the abscess subsides; then set it equal to the humerus as you can easily and skillfully, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration where there are fractures; then bind, as necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 If there are fractures in the bone, if it is of two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or at your hand if it is a small member, or with two strings, or with one string and at your hand; then set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are dislocated, reset them by all means, and be careful in your work not to cause injury or pain to the patient; and adjust well the two joints of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that they are not correctly aligned: straighten them nicely, and do not strain or press too much as those who force it out by their work produce abscesses and contractions in the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is set, take good care to keep the patient still, neither awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and be sure that the limb is as secure as possible so it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 If it does not feel pain, then it is not set and you must put it in such a position that it does not feel any pain; and be sure that it is set straight, so twisting does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb depends on this as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small members such as fingers and toes; you must wrap them with fine, soft linen cloths; and for the large ones like thighs and legs: you must wrap them with a wide, hard rope because the wide ropes encompass the entire large limb evenly and hold it equally all around so there is no swelling; then tie three or four turns of thread lightly around the rope, and grasp a little part of the rope with your hand, then go above the break and tighten less than the break, then move a little away from the break; and soften the rope a little at a time, until you take a large part of the healthy flesh; then take another rope, and turn it around in reverse over the broken limb; then return to the area below the break, and tighten it moderately, not too strong or too loosely as we have said in the first instruction above; then put linen or cloth pieces between the ropes, until they are all even, then tie them all together with a bandage, and then place well-made splints on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is an abscess or boil, place warm compresses on it to alleviate the abscess, and let it stay for some days; then apply hot iron rods, half the size of a large cane, or pliers like those used to cut wood, in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 The iron rods that are placed on the wound should be slightly larger and thicker than the others; and they should also be as long as necessary for the small or large member; then apply the hot rods in the same way as you have done with the first injury, then attach a thread to it, similar to the one used in the first instruction on the wound; the thread should be moderate in thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax yarn; for if the thread is too thick, like those who make ropes from twisted flax, it is a great error because the knot cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it should not have less space than the width of a dove's eye.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pierced by the limbs of the ribs after setting them in healthy bones, place linen or flax padding beneath them to prevent swelling.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is broken and the nerves are torn, I will tell the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to hold bones of broken members all day long on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to set bones before five or seven days, or more according to your certainty of the abscess healing; and here is the ancient method for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: it is that you take flour kept near the mill walls, mix it with much egg, and apply this paste, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it; and this is the common method of setting bones in many ways, and equally for women and small children, as it is not either too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for healing breaks, dislocations and twists: take albaries, lupine, elm, asafetida and Arabic gum, mix in ten parts; add myrrh and aloes, five parts; seven parts of alkali; then make a powder and mix with yolk of an egg; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition and quickly heals broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method for setting fractures that is effective against twists: take mugwort and wormwood, one part each; myrrh and aloes, nine parts each; acacia bark six parts; Armenian bole, ten parts; grind well, mix with vinegar or much egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another method of splinting for joints and dislocated bones, alleviating the pain that occurs, and treating it with cutting of the bone and breaking: take new linen, wet it in warm water and oil, and place it on the joint or bone.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not heal, but it is good for alleviating abscess pain and bone fracture pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of setting broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth wormwood, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of plaster for the healing of the broken bone and for promoting the healing of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take the root of vismalve, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of beans, of each one part; grind and mix with wine, and if the members are scalded, mix with moist coriander water or vinegar, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of amputation stronger than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of mallow, flax, balm, clover, and sage, and violet and camomile flowers, all one part; grind and concoct with salt water, sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that no other substance besides a mixture of beeswax and oil should be applied to a broken limb for restoration, and it should neither be too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen states that for restoring a broken limb, one should apply warm dry substances such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of application that is useful for wounds and pain: take mugath (possibly a type of plant) and chopped human hair or feathers of birds, and vis amalgam (a substance used in medicine), grind them all together to make a poultice and apply it to the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then untie a little later, and make sure the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if it is untied by many days, and pain comes to the place, or inflammation without rest or swelling, then hasten, and untie it, and remove the amputation immediately; and take a light cloth, seawater-soaked sponge, and dip in water, and raise the wound until the inflammation ceases, and soothe the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then cover with dry linen moistened with water or rose oil, and bind above a nut, until you are sure of abscess heat; and let the inflammation of the member rest, and soothe the pain, then continue the binding subtly, and a little amputation, and do not strain it too much as before; and make it subtle until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess has burst, become red, painful and swollen, and if you need plaster and linen, then suture it as you did before evenly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 If no swelling comes to the member as we have said, do not dislocate it before three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, as one sees, until the break heals and approaches the bone again; then hold it more firmly than before, and fatten its flesh, as I have said before; if you see the joint drying out too much, know that nourishment cannot enter; therefore give him warm, moist heat, every time you dislocate it, and stretch a little the ligament; by this work, cut off the nourishment from the member, and heal quickly what the foolish doctor leaves twisted: this is bad, and this work is dangerous, and I see nothing else but laziness and working incorrectly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	diverse methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many kinds of fractures are, and they have various shapes, and the causes are determined; because there are fractures made by sword blow, and the collum bone breaks the entire bone up to the shaft that is beneath the bone, as a cleaver or wedge does; and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	or the sword strikes the bone from above by piercing it and this type of fracture is called "complete"; and the wound caused by these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a bruise filled with blood, or a wound or arrow wounds, or falling upon a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If it is a swelling that approaches the membrane underneath the bone, or it is on the bone and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that penetrates the bone as thinly as a hair, and it makes a small crack, and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, falling, or something similar, and causes the piece of bone to enter inside, and the fracture lines are like a blacksmith when he hammers on a pot; if the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more often in those who have a moist bone in the head, such as in a child's head; and it occurs in all these ways of breaking that small pieces are dislodged, as in shards; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breaks by the drawing on them, and the testing inquiry, and through the corruption of flesh that is above. (line-by-line translation)
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of the capillary is known by those who, when the bone is exposed and scraped above, if the break appears black. (line-by-line translation)
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, take care of the patient's circumstances, and if you see any bad accident, as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, stretching, swelling, fever, the hairs coming out and reddening, and other symptoms in various dispositions, it cannot heal with doubt. (line-by-line translation)
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an overwhelming accident, and you hope for salvation, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the splinter first comes to you in winter, it must be removed before the fourteenth day at the bone's mouth.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not rot, and the accidents we have mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 If the break in the bone reaches up to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must cut the affected area as follows: take hold of the patient's head and expose the bone on all sides as much as possible, and on the edge of the wound, press gently so that blood or abscess does not appear; prepare cloths dampened with rose oil; and have them ready to apply pressure when necessary. Then fill the area around the bone with damp cloths, and wait until the swelling is relieved, ensuring no more bleeding occurs; then begin to remove the bone using one of two methods: the first method is to make a shallow cut across, forming an "X" shape.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then insert another, larger incision.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various sizes of blades, some narrow and others wide, sharp and made of iron not copper; and work lightly so as not to pierce the flesh.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and projecting, it is necessary that you pierce around it so that you provide blades with grooves, not sharp enough to penetrate beyond the bone surface, and above the point there should be a margin or circle that prevents the point from passing beyond the bone; and you must have several of them, each coming in its place at the depth of the bone, so that you have grooved blades for all cases; and this is the form of the four types of grooved blades:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place one grooved blade on the bone and turn it with your hand until you feel the bone is pierced; then move the blade to another part a little afterward, and do this all around; then cut the space of the bone between the periosteum, and do this as delicately as possible, lightly, as we have said, until you extract the bone or any of the tools you have, such as pliers or forceps; and make sure you do not touch the cerebral membrane or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you remove the splinter that has remained in the bone with an instrument resembling a pick, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other picks; and if anything remains of the small bones or scales, lightly remove them with the instruments; then treat the wound with cautery and ointment as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of work, which is more secretive, is the one that the Greeks call it, and they highly praise it, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture moves open; so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place it under the head of this concave incisor, as shown in the following figure:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 Do not cut it in half, and the piece is split into two sides, so that the saw is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer from above, so that you gently break the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is below; if it is pierced through to the bone, remove it gently, for one can easily break it without causing harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the membrane, and the bone is only split from above, and there are small fragments, then after smoothing it, remove the scales with a sharp rasp, having different amounts as necessary, in order to provide the most suitable amount for each place, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with a large rasp, then proceed with finer ones, and do not stop until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-like or subtle fractures, you must provide a treatment according to its nature; and this is not something that can be answered by one who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the wound is exposed, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled over once or twice, wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; do this gently so as not to burden the wound, then administer more linen thread above it, but do not tighten it more than enough to cover the wound only; leave it like that for a day or two until the abscesses are calmed down, then remove it and administer medicines such as root of lilies, flour of wheat, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; from these things make powder and put it on the wound, and immediately administer non-bitter medicines; and ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment or pus collected, for when pus collects on the wound cover, it can rot and cause great harm to the patient, as when something biting is put on the wound, it can burn through above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Then take care, if any harmful event befalls the patient as we have said, it is full of doubtful meaning.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if blackness does not come violently except by medicine that has been applied to it, and it possesses such virtue, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in wax the cloth, and put it on the wound; then treat it according to the methods of treatment required until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or only one of them, since they are two bones, but the one below is cartilage and does not break, unless it causes a swelling or deformation, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, you must swallow your little thumb or finger, and put it equal to the break in the thumb indentation, and at the joint by the back, until the thumb grows according to its natural figure; do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain due to your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part near the neck and the thumb cannot reach its place, you must align it with the head of a ruler, a little bigger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two parts, then do the same and hasten to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then graft linen bandages at the tip of the thumb where the break is located.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you step on another person or are stepped upon, it breaks [the bone] and the tendons become as thick as they fill the nostrils with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said any remedy that one must moisten tents with butter, and churn every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It doesn't seem good to me, but it is necessary that they are moistened in an egg yolk concoction and flour powder; then leave the tendon until the bone is hard and the cartilages are tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one steps on feathers of goose in place of tendons, and if it is wrapped with a piece of linen, and holds the breakage, and blows warm air [into it]; then do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the new (opening) while you are working on it, put either beeswax or cotton wool soaked in rose oil, or a small piece of lignum aloes, there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If abscesses do not open on their own, apply a plaster outside made from wheat flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk; then put light poultices over it and do not tie them too tight; if the break in the neck is small and broken into many pieces, remove them using suitable instruments; then stitch the wound, and treat it with healing ointments and salves suitable for that purpose; if there is no wound within the neck, cure the tendons, and put cotton swabs inside until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the break is only displaced and not broken through to the inside, but rather bent within, this can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the patient's mouth; if it is on the left side, you should put your index finger of the right hand and push gently into the break, then use the other hand to adjust it from the outside and align it.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is dislocated in two places, then you must administer extension of two parts, equal in size.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If the teeth move or are broken, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a splint on the fractured jaw and put a double cloth over it; put a large and well-made cradle or piece of leather equal to the jaw lengthwise and crosswise, and secure it as you can, and command the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see the figure change, dislocate it on the third day and then reset it to its original position; put a poultice on top made with flour or wheat with egg, after removing the splint; put a light linen bandage over the poultice and if the dislocation reoccurs, leave it as long as it is healed; many times it heals in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, bring what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is breakage and wound together, take care that no piece of the bone is removed; use the tools suitable for that purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, you should widen it with fire as necessary.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, close the wound if it is wide, and put on one dressing suitable for that purpose, to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	From the lock (or fastening)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The lock (or fastening) breaks many times in front of the shoulder, and the breakage is in four ways: or it is broken and dislocated in two places, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operations are when the break is without wound, that you have two assistants, so one grips the shoulder where the lock feels broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then put the break in equal alignment with your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and has no appearance or bulging.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, put a round cushion of cloth or linen under the patient's shoulder, and let it be thick according to your necessity; stretch and lift the lock, and hold the cushion with your hand, so that you align the break as needed.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder out of the joint because it comes in completely, then the patient must lie on their affected side, and a small pillow should be placed under the shoulder, and the attendant should push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the socket is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find broken bones, then it is necessary that you cut across them; and pull the pieces gently apart, and if the bone cannot be joined due to any obstruction, strike it at one of the incisions you made; but place this instrument under the socket to keep it open.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And it should resemble a spoon, not pointed, and be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and let it have two points, as you see, and one wide, and the other narrow, as is the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones; and when you are certain that the abscess has been pierced through, if the opening is small, or if you doubt that the abscess has been pierced through, use linen and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If abscess heating comes, wet linen in rose oil and asafoetida and vinegar, then place on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The setting of a bone fracture with wounds and cuts is as follows: you place the padding made from powdered millstone and egg yolk on the bone, then put light stops over it, and if needed, put a splint under the injury; then take a very wide bandage, about a palm's width, then put two layers of linen over the stops, and the padding; then take a thin strip of wood three fingers wide and long, wrap it around that wide bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang out; and place the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the injury and the sick person's neck; and tighten each part, and when you see that the injury is holding the fracture well, and you clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, you should check it every day, and when the linens loosen, you should tighten it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the injury to lift the shoulder up; the swelling of the fracture will subside due to the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, until 20 days have passed; then resume the padding, if necessary, and tighten it and leave it in place until it is healed; and it will heal within 28 days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 It happens that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated and only treatment can be applied through touch; if it appears according to the shape of the break, and it is reset according to its natural form in all ways possible; then put powder from the mill with a lot of egg white, light bandages, and put it on the linen cloth; then put on top a wide and thin stick, about a little larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hollows anywhere on the shoulder, fill those hollows with flax bandages so that the stick fits equally; then bind it firmly and tightly in one great bend, so that the stick does not move from its place, and watch it daily; and every time it softens, bind it again, adjusting the stick if it is out of its place, and make the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is completed, release it, and be careful because it is not easy for a bone to move lightly back into place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front and not below the skin, lift it up, remove the bone, and do as we have said in the fracture of the fistula to treat an abscess by heating.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the fistula
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The limb is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens seldom; however, it often breaks at the joint.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken at the joint, it declines below, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of alignment, and immediately, and sometimes vomits blood, and the fracture opens in the bone broken, and he feels it all over.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back with their head down, and one cushion is placed between the shoulders, then the shoulders are pressed and the ribs are brought together to your hands, and it must be done carefully so that the bone figure is as required; then salt poultice and bandages are put on top of the broken bone, or a light cloth, and it is wrapped in one cloth, and it is tied to the broken bone so that it does not move; and you turn the limb roundabout, and tighten it gradually, and check each hour if it heals, and if it softens, tighten again; and if it needs to be dislocated due to corrosion or inflammation at the location, or pain or abscess, hurry up, and dislocate it, remove the poultice, and address those who came with ways of treatment; then reattach the poultice, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of a broken rib
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs occurs only in large ones behind the back and in the chest, and they do not break easily except due to moisture; and it is well felt at the inquiry with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the treatment is to set the break as necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply a splint and tie it with a stick if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break in the ribs is sinking inside, the patient feels intense pain and shortness of breath, similar to pleurisy, for the bone punctures the lining; and the edges are sharp, and immediately he vomits a large amount of blood, which is serious illness, and the ancients have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the break outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot poultices come, unless they have arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have arrived, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that someone should put leeches on the wound to drain pus, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the leech does not attract excess fluid to the wound due to its weak constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that someone should cover the wound with damp linen soaked in hot oil and put bandages between the ribs to even out the swelling around it; then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain in the bone that does not bear fabric, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut through the rib on the side of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument under it to prevent dislocation; then you must split the bone, remove it gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with splints until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if abscesses swell up, put oil-soaked woolen cloths on it and place it there; and cure the area of the abscess as needed; and let the patient lie down on the side where it is, until it drains.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes the bones in the neck break and do not bend; and similarly with the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when it happens to anyone, and you wish to know if it will heal or not, take notice if the hands become softened, swollen and dead, and he cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortal in various positions, and if the joint does not move or feel when stretched or pricked, know that the bone joint is saved, and the patient should be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if a similar thing happens in the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, take care if the feet are numb, and if there are accidents that are in hand, and above the back there is a sudden jump and movement without intention; and when it is brought onto its belly, it jumps and moves without intention.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is brought onto its stomach and it wants to lie down, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is fatal: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this incident does not happen to him, it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you anoint [the abscess] with rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is soothed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters and tie it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the part where they feel pain, until it heals.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone is dislocated, it should be covered [with something]; then remove the bone, join the two edges of the wound with stitches if it is large, and treat the wound with healing salve until it heals; and if the head of the bone (which is called "the heads of the cow") is broken, take your left hand, put it on the dislocated part and hold it equal to your right hand, then apply the plaster and the linen bandage, if you have them; then tighten [the bandage], and if there are bones protruding, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ankle bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it occurs, there is only a little lessening of the pain at the site; and it extends along the length, bends towards the crotch, causes pain and swelling at the site that breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the healing is that you extend your hand above [the break], so that you are over the break; and recognize where the break is and what its shape is; and if the break is only at the top, then set the break equal to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is along the length or it bends inward, make the patient lie on his stomach so that the healing of the break comes to your attention.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it (the dislocation) right, put an armature on it, then put a splint of wood or horn over it and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the lever below the ribs until the patient is comfortable.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess comes to the surface, do not touch it until the abscess has calmed down, and place what we have previously mentioned on it; then return to treatment, and hold it as necessary, if there is no bad occurrence; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is the part that is between the neck and the arm, and if it is fractured, it should be restored according to one of the two ways: of which one is that you take a rod filled with coarse material, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the rod to each other and raise them up, and place the patient on one seat; then drop the broken arm onto the rod, until it reaches the level, and have a hump in the rod, then raise something heavy above it or the assistants extend it downwards; then place the hands of the molder on the fracture equally, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that you lay the patient on his bed, tie one end of the rod to his neck and command two assistants that one holds the part above the fracture with their hands, and the other holds both ends of the rod, each pulling in their respective directions.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the ligament beneath the break and above the break, and extend each of the attendants to their respective parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the neck of the shoulder, then you must place the splint beneath the neck and the other side towards the break; and similarly, if the break is towards the neck, you should lightly place the splint without labor, until the break is level with the neck and with the skin; then make it level, as required, and hold it in place, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess does come, do not hold it for more than seven days, and put a soft cloth in oil of roses on it to soothe the abscess; then hold it, and the method of holding it is that you place the plaster on the break, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and put the towel, and hold it onto the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm is in its correct position, unless anything prevents it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone is moving, use wedges, and put a larger and stronger wedge on the break than the others, and have one space between each wedge, and let each wedge be so large that it passes the break two fingers width from each side; then hold onto the wedges, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the break, with more force but less in pulling away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 If you see the bones set and the bandage tightened, as we have said, during the time you are restoring a broken limb, and you doubt the abscess has formed, then leave it to heal for seven days, as we have said; then look every three days at the binding, to ensure that swelling does not occur at the site or the blood vessels do not come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 If no such accidents occur, do not remove the dislocation before three days or more, and let the patient lie on his back, with his hands on his stomach; put a clean cushion of linen equally under the shoulder, and watch every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the ligaments are not softened; by the virtue of medicine, direct it, and give him the food as previously specified, in such a way that the meat is initially subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be repositioned within forty days of the accident; and then it must be dislocated again and warm water and ointments given to direct it.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the structure is deformed and swollen, it remains to dissolve (or loosen) for days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	on the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones, which are called the "two shafts"; one is small, and it is the one that forms the elbow; the other is large, and it is the one below, near the little finger; sometimes only the large shaft breaks, or sometimes both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small fissures are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; but when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more difficult than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small fissure that is broken, it should be slightly stretched and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large fissure, it should be stretched more firmly; and extend above the cussin (or finger), and raise the little finger of the hand higher than the others, and the small ones lower than the others, and cross the patient over himself, and the cussin in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then stretch the assistants arms below to the affected part or the ligament, and one assistant on the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then equalize the shoulder, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no dislocation that pricks the bone, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut off and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If with the break at the joint, I have spoken of it in the individual chapter; then take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 If at the beginning of healing pusules appear, spread the bandage made of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; attach the bandage carefully until the pusules are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 Then remove the wax, and put the plaster of the powder from the mill with plenty of egg, afterwards place the splints, and the splint at the breakage point should be more prominent, and a little wider than the others; and know that it should have 6 splints or more in different positions: whether the breakage is in one bone or two; and bind above the breakage more than elsewhere, and always less when pulling, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and may the bandages over the breakage be soft and moist, not hard nor harsh; and may the thread, which is used to bind it, be made of flax, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And keep the limb and the joint immobilized for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.
