And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itch that happens on the limb, you must irrigate the limb with hot water, until the itching subsides; and let the limb not rest at all.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 Then resume the immobilization, and if the joints are weakened and the bones dislocated, as in similar cases, advise accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the urine cannot reach the member due to it being too narrow, then you must soften it with oil for a few days, until the urine passes through, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things that we have mentioned happen to the patient, do not discharge them for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 In addition to this, have the patient hold their hands at their neck, and let their necks be even, and guard against movement and displacement, and sleep on their back; know that this fracture will heal in thirty or forty days, or perhaps twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the remedies.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	For at the back of the hand and the fingers, there are few fractures, but it occurs repeatedly many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is fractured or dislocated, the patient should lie flat on his back, with arms straight and evenly aligned; then he places his hand on a stretched cloth, and the attendant extends the broken bones and aligns them as much as possible; then apply plaster and compresses, if abscess does not occur; then apply a splint according to the severity of the fracture; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the side of the sole near the abdomen, make a splint from cloths, and instruct the patient to press his injured hand against it; then bind it with a long piece of cloth, and the splint should be as large as the palm of the hand, and tightened as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the edge, you must place a splint above and another beneath in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie it all around the hand and stop the flow of blood between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the break comes on any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, equalize it as necessary; hold it with the sole and, if you see that it is displaced, place a straight splint to lift the break and immobilize it; if the break is in the other fingers (such as the index or another), equalize them and tie them with the healthy finger that follows; tie all of them in one binding, which is enough, or place a splint, such as a thumb-splint; take care in restoring and positioning the abscess, and apply heat to it as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the leg are often broken, and one sees it when it twists forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one ties a ligament above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients lie on their face, then each attendant extends their ligament equally to its part; and this is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is close to the root of the shinbone, it is one of the ligaments towards the joint, and the other ligaments on the side of the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And if it is close to the knee, then it will be the ligaments near the knee and the extensions below; then hold the bone equal to its two hands, according to its natural shape, and then place the splint and the bandage, until abscess does not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that heats up, let it cool down first, then return to your work and treatment; the ligature is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 You should wrap above the fracture with bandages double in one or two layers, and remove the excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and push a long thread between the shinbone and the leg, below, beneath the knee; and bring the head of the thread up; then turn the leg and the bandage up, then place splints on the fracture, and a splint on the bone of the leg; then use soft cloth for seven inches between the leg and the thigh to equalize the tension, then start to bind firmly three or four times over the fracture; and as you go higher above the fracture, do not tighten it; then take the two threads that you put in place between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return to below the head of the thread, so that you come under the foot; tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, until no abscess or inflammation or any similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a break, straighten it as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they must be cut off if possible; and if it cannot be done, the limb must be broken and the bone removed; and cure it as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken so that it can be splinted like in the shoulder or arm; however, in this kind of restoration, the patient does not feel pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored within a few days, either less or more, according to the various complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the groin region, there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 If it breaks, it is not so much a fracture, but rather a crack or perforation, and it causes all kinds of pain and injury, and this is felt very much.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when one equalizes the bone that is broken at its ends, as long as it can be assembled; then put the splint, and place a round peg there if needed, and tighten it as required, then recheck all the arrangements mentioned in other breaks, such as an abscess, boil or similar; for each accident, use what is required until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right "hammer", and the other is called "shinbone"; and it breaks in a similar way as in the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the procedure is the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 If the large bone (femur) is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; and it twists beneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply extension, make it even, and tie the bones equally; however, if the fracture is ugly or there are more pieces, the extension should be lesser and lighter; align accordingly to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two fists full of splints that support the leg on both sides and are as long as the length of the leg from the knee to below; then wrap them in two layers, one above and one below, and tie them at this point, and the leg will not be able to decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should provide a splint as long as the leg, and it should be of wood, and they place the leg on it to prevent movement, and properly make this in the fracture where there is pain; and move the leg every day to see if there is any abscess or other accident; and cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but there may be fracture of the bones in the foot and toes, and it has no cure except for compression in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones in the foot, and you see these bones protruding one above the other, place the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wants to walk, then place your foot under his, where the bones are raised, and press them back into their places; then apply the splint and padding, and put a small table under the foot with two flat surfaces, then tighten it around the foot in the appropriate way; once you have wrapped the cloths around it, and other things that you may need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, remove the splint, because you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two [bones] are broken, restore them as we have said in the hand bones; then place a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and it should be slightly larger; then place a wooden block beneath the fractured one, as I have said, and hold it aligned; and if there are two or more, or more, break each bone separately, place a splint over each one according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the wooden block under the fracture; and ensure that the head of the block is facing the abdomen of the limb, so it covers it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, from what we have said; and treat each accident as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of nature (the womb) is broken, make it enlarged, then incline it towards the small of the back and hold it from behind; fill the belly of the woman with linen cloth and also as thick as possible; then turn the woman, lift her legs little by little, and pull the cloth out until it reaches the opening of the womb, and the bone comes out with the linen cloth; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cloth, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or longer: the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of straw, and tie a string to one end, and blow all the bladder into the womb; then inflate the string forcefully, until the bladder is inflated inside: the womb will return to its position; fill it with linen cloth and leave it for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the arm bone is broken for either man or woman, restore it as we have said in the wrist bone; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from him who applies his study and skill to them, and pay heed to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 The term "fracture" refers to various ways of the restoration: therefore, understand me.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take an owl's gullet and insert the penis; then wrap it in cloth and leave it for 3 days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	with break (or fracture) and wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For that person who has a fracture with a wound (or break with wound), especially if it is large as the leg bone or shoulder blade or similar, it should be cauterized now, as the cauteries that we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, it should be sealed with vitriol (a disinfectant), if you have no other option, then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour, or on that day, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess bursts, allow the healing to continue until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is appeased; do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks open in the hollow of the cavity, you must set it gently and slightly extend it.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not aligned for you to set it evenly in your hands, you will need this tool made of iron that has 7 or 8 inches long and its width according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the mirror that he holds .3 or 4, depending on what is needed in each cure of breaking bones; and it should be round and slightly larger than a coin so it does not bend under compression on the member during your work, and sharp before, and thick from the middle to the tip, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "wrist", so the curved bones should be placed on top of the prominent bone (the head of the radius); and press down once until it aligns, one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 If the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then cut the head of the bone so that the instrument can take hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot return the bone as we have said, if you have an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, use it to your power; then gnaw that which is left in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Then place it back in its proper position, then moisten the cloth in black stiptic vinegar, and do this if it is warm; and do not put any ointment or other substance on the wound where there is oil, because it causes pus and corruption to come; then administer ice when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound exposed, and cover it with a covering according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted by the fracture; and many times this has been done by foolish healers, causing illness or death in some cases; and the bandaging should be softer and more flexible than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident might come from it, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, do not put splints on it; but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And after a day or two, if you see pus boiling at the wound, take away what you have put on it and put healing ointment on it, such as tetraformulation and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be prepared in such a way that the splints slide downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they pass many days without healing and continue to swell again, know that there are small bone fragments; therefore, you must carefully open the wound and remove all the dislocated fragments causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the site, or any other kind of corruption, you must treat it, as he said in the chapter before this one.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and open above the member, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and similar in large members, do not draw it out because many times death comes from it; but let it be as it is until it can heal; perhaps after 20 or 30 days, it may close by itself; then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	broken bones that come on the suture (joint)
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after health following the break, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a pitiful sight to see the shape of the limb; and unfortunately, the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take good care of it afterwards: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and saracocola, acacia, and similar others, taking any one of these substances or all together and boil them in a stiptic wine or with an abundance of egg or with oil; then place the mixture in a bandage and apply pressure and do not remove it for many days; then dislocate it, and start another, until the nodulation is removed; or you hold above a piece of wood well made; for the properties of wood are that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, chop it off, and make the excess apparent; or you shave it at any razor until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb that is weak after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is set and remains afterwards, the limbs become weak and delicate; this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nutrients could not reach the member; or due to excessive swelling; or due to excessive movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body strong, until the flesh multiplies in him; then provide baths, and give him joy and rest; next apply salve to the member, so that the salve attracts great nutrients, and often apply cold water to it, until the nutrients reach the member; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the limb is disfigured, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the foolish who say that one should break the limb anew, and many fools have done this in our land; and this practice is condemned, and it causes great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the knots and tortures are fresh, they must be softened with hot water or softening herbs such as vismalve leaves, root radishes, sweet clovers, and similar things; and you should make a soothing plaster using dyaquilon well-made, and take musk from vismalve, mix it with gelyn grease or sesame oil, and apply the plaster; or you can take greased figs, grind them with corn bran, and similar medicines that alleviate pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes, the dislocation is opened by continuous and prolonged rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortures are hardened and strengthened like stone, requiring surgery, it must be covered up to the bone, at the subtle incision; and cotton and wool should be placed in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	If dislocation occurs in anyone, it must now be repositioned with care.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if you wait, the joint swells, and inadvertently if it is reset at that point; therefore, it should not be moved when it is swollen: many times it brings spasms and other pains; however, when this occurs, let the patient bleed, then leave it alone until the abscesses have calmed down; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently manipulate it, and treat each limb as needed according to its location.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of shoulder dislocations from head to feet.
des mandibules	of jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	1. Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous: It happens that the jaws are dislocated in two ways: either they are partly dislocated from their place and softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards down, causing saliva to flow from the mouth which it cannot hold, and it cannot close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return in various positions more often.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 If it is whole and complete, you must quickly reset it and not hesitate; and in such a way that the attendant holds the head of the patient, and places one of his fingers at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is from two parts; and the other hand should be spread out, to make it even; and command the patient to soften their jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And bring the thumb equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the reset is difficult, similarly, if it is both jaws together, apply hot water and oil to loosen them gently; do not rush to forcefully move, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they (the dislocated limbs) are put back into place again, and the patient's mouth is closed well with soft bandages made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with several strings; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be placed between two cushions, so that he does not move either to the right or to the left, nor makes any effort to exert himself, but takes light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are closed; and then eat lightly whatever he wants, and do not force himself to open his mouth to eat or drink, until the jaws are well healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be reset in an hour and are not returned to their place, fever and usual sweats occur, and perhaps abdominal swelling, and possibly vomiting bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	When you see this, therefore, know that it is disaster; and many times the one in whom it occurs dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the collarbone   (metaphorical usage, meaning "neck" or "throat")
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The splint cannot dislocate from the side within the ribcage and is dislocated outside once at the hip, and it is felt clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back with his arms stretched out; then press firmly at the joint with your palm, and it will return; then place the splint and bandage on it and hold it in place; the shoulder which is towards the cost cannot dislocate again; if it does, reset it to its place, as we have said; then place the splint and bandage on it and hold it in place, and tell the patient to rest until he is well; and the same applies when the shoulder of the back is dislocated, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 The shoulder can dislocate in three ways: one is that it dislocates at the socket below; the second is to the hip part; and by accident, it dislocates above, which happens rarely; it does not dislocate behind due to the shoulder nor inside through the nerves; and it often dislocates below towards the socket in those who have little flesh, for it can easily pop out; but in those with sufficient flesh, it can jump out slightly and return slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	Sometimes happens to some men percussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must verify it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocations are when they move downwards towards the socket, and you will find a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and beneath the socket, touching the top of the shoulder, just as in an eye; and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its place, nor move it at all; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly touching; and this kind of dislocation is not always difficult to reset, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The minister lifts the patient's hand high, then puts your fist underneath it, and pulls the joint up forcefully to its place; and the minister lifts the hand and stretches it high, then puts it underneath; quickly it will come back.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 If the dislocation does not come as we have said in hand's breadth after some days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and they should be given soothing and softening balm, such as a decoction of elder and fenugreek and melilot in water, and it should be applied; then make the patient lie on their back, and put a piece of linen cloth equal in size but not too soft nor too hard under the socket; then place your foot on the cloth, and carefully lift the sick shoulder; and another minister holds the top of the shoulder, so that it does not move downwards; the shoulder immediately returns to its place, and if you find that you reset it in this manner: it is necessary for a man larger than the patient to be present; he should stand upright facing the side, and push the sick shoulder under the socket of the patient, lifting the socket upwards so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the patient's hand downward towards their abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, he cannot hold anything heavy, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And you can also reset it in another way: and it is done by inserting a long needle into the ground, so that the head is as round as a pea, but not too thick or too thin; then it should be placed under the patient, but he should have a linen cloth beneath him, and he should be standing tall against the post; then his hand should be extended to the other side, forming a hole, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return due to all these things that we said, you should perform this treatment: take a needle from two strong hands and four fingers wide, which has a round head to enter fully into the hole, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie the head of the stick with cloth to prevent the patient from being scalded, then insert the stick into the anus of the patient; extend one arm along the stick, and bind the shoulder to the stick, and the forearm at the end of the hand, then place one leg on one side of a bench, and let the other side hang loose; the dislocation will be reduced immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is inside, no matter how, you must put a sphere of cotton equal in size under the anus, then place a plaster filled with powder from the mill, along with incense and egg yolk, all over the shoulder and around; then hold it down beneath the anus, turn the string around the plaster, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little food, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal faster; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is hardened and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture or for another reason, you should administer fire cauterization at three places as stated in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you have done all of this and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve to the shoulder is cut or stretched out or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation towards the hip and limbs, front or back, is caused by force and extension of hands, and other means are administered for its treatment; it should be cured until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing, if there is still pain in the limb and slow movement, the patient should use baths several times until the pain subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost   (This line seems incomplete, as it does not seem to follow the pattern of translation from the previous lines.)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the arm is dislocated at points, and it comes back at points; and if it becomes dislocated from all sides, both in front and behind, and the dislocation is not repaired because it can be seen clearly and felt clearly; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when joining the broken bone with the healthy one, make sure it can be seen clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the dislocated joint cannot bend the arm nor touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset the dislocation in such a way that the abscesses come out easily, for if the abscess comes out, it would be difficult to set; and perhaps it cannot be set completely from all sides, especially when it is at the back; it is worth more than other dislocations, and it causes greater pain, and perhaps death follows.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is as follows, when it can be returned to its state, extend your hand to both of his hands; and stretch out his arms, and place his hands opposite each other according to the bone joints outside and inside, and push the joint back to its sockets or to the root of his palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will return when you fold your hand over your other hand, and push against the bone joint that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 If it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and it is that two people should extend the arm and hold it in place while it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from both sides, when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth around it; and when the healer has joined the dislocated joint with his hand, apply some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint back into its place as much as possible until it returns; and when it is in its place, apply dry plaster with egg white and hold it firmly, and let the arm hang from the neck of the patient for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is held in place, you unbind it and leave it. If you see that the joint is not holding well, you repeat the plaster and binding, and leave it like that for some days until it is firmly set; then you unbind it again.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 If it feels sore after the reset of the joint and it becomes stiff, wash and rub it well, press until it is soothed; or you put a sheep's woolen cloth dampened with butter on the joint, then leave for a day and a night, then remove it, and make it enter water again; and when it sweats, wipe the joint gently, then place the cloth back, then enter it in water again; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, put warm moist cow's dung on top of it and strain it; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand joint, and its reset is easy, more than other jointures, nonetheless it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour when it is dislocated, before the joint is swollen or there comes an abscess hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 When the hand is dislocated, you must place the affected hand on a table, and extend your fingers so that the patient places his palm above the appearance of the joint, and push it until it returns to its original position. Then, you should ensure that it is properly aligned; then, the patient puts the back of his hand on a table for stretching and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, place the patient's dorsal side of his hand on the table, and hold your hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, it's good. But if not, apply a plaster to soothe the abscess, and leave it like that to start healing.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if it cannot be endured and you are unable to put it back within any days, the dislocated joint remains twisted; it does not hurt the patient that much as long as his hand is injured and cannot exert any force: know then that the nerves or arteries are severed, or there's no other remedy but to straighten with a surgical cautery and possibly nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at its place, put a splint on it as we have said, then bind and leave for 5 days, then unbind and leave in this manner.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot be moved well and there is no pain, moist with warm water and rub until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers on the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then you must push the dislocation back into place until it returns, then hold the finger's head and turn it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and make it straight in that day; and tie it as we have said, and untie it by day, and make it move, and bind it again; and do this often until it becomes tight, and similarly do this if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and similarly do this when it is dislocated from other places.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	And for the dislocation of the small of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the small of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are many such dislocations without a cure, death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that the evacuations leap unintentionally, and it cannot be held, and many times a member becomes softened, or one of the two legs or the two arms, or the spine; which becomes mute at four parts, this is called "gilbositez"; the cure is that you examine if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if it has not healed or been cured since then.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And that which comes from falling or strikes or similar things, the old ways of cures spoke in great words, but there is not much benefit in all this; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the hump that comes before, there is no remedy or healing; and similarly the one that comes directly on both sides, and can only be cured by the one that comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the patient should lie face down in one place, and have support underneath him, so he does not bleed; then insert the iron rod into the hump at the base, and another one at the feet, and tie a rope over the patient's shoulders, and another around the legs, and knees, and ankles; and two assistants know the ropes, one at the hump and others at the feet, among the two iron rods; and they should be tightly secured, the rods as we have said, and the ministers place their palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if the dislocation does not return with this cure, take a table three feet long and hollow it out below, have the patient lie on their side, and push the top of the table beneath the opening, then place the middle part of the table on the spine; put your feet on the other end of the table and press hard, until it returns to its place. If you see, do the same with a pulley that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 Then you put two needles of a large size in the patient's head, one on each side, and leave a palm's length of space between each needle; have a hole through each needle, where the pulley turns, and keep the needles firmly in the ground so they do not move; between the two needles, have a moving needle, like a cable, and have two small needles of a palm's length, to turn the pulley. Then take the rope that passes through the needles and attach it to the pulley near the head, and the other rope to the pulley at the feet, and each servant turns their pulley along the entire rope, and the master equalizes the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it [the dislocation] is evened out, apply a drying plaster with egg white, then bandage it, and then use a splint of a tablet three feet long, which penetrates the diseased part and the healthy part of the spine; then tie it with a cord as we have said, and let the patient rest gently until he is well; and if any thing comes at the end of his healing, administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the splint that we have mentioned earlier; and sometimes a piece of wood may be administered, and sometimes the appearance occurs in the lower spine of the back, and it is thought to be dislocations; and this is the bone that opens, which should not make anyone assume: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the shoulder and the arm joints come out of place only by dislocations themselves, not otherwise as with other joints; and the shoulder joint is dislocated in four ways: inside and outside, front and back; and more on the inside than elsewhere, and less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of his dislocation within [the body] is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer and opens wider the sick person's knees than the healthy ones; and the sick cannot bend their knees in fire; and it is the joint that is dislocated by swelling due to abscess, since the thighbone comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that one who suffers from this condition is that this event happens contrary to what was mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that one whose leg is swollen as mentioned before, are that it is not doubled in the knee, and does not feel pain when bent, and if you wish to make it walk, it cannot move forward, and holds back its urine, and the ankle inflates, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that one whose condition is at the back, are that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it double, and this leg is twisted more than the other, and the ankle becomes softened, and the head of the thighbone is beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The re-alignments of this similarity of dislocation are such that you should observe if the dislocations are old and remain in their position without any treatment; and it is not appropriate for there to be any assumption about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	For one whose dislocation is recent, and there are four types of dislocation, you should hurry that you turn the joint, push it inward and outward, and move it left and right; by chance if it returns, no further treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must summon a strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with both hands or by a rope tied above the knee; another minister stretches his hand thus that he puts his hands under the knees, then binds a sturdy rope above the thigh; another one grips the rope of the thigh; and all extend upwards and downwards together, until the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If the shoulder is not in place, treatment must be applied to its appearance. When a dislocation is at the front, you must remember to have the patient lie on his healthy side. Then tie a rope around the thigh's root, and the leg that is under the angle, then pull the rope towards the angle and the hip; then take another assistant to hold the large leg of the diseased thigh and stretch it out backwards in shape: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 If you cannot fix it in this way as we have said, then you must tie the feet of the patient with a strong cord above both ankles and knees, and the sick leg should be extended two fingers more than the other; then hang him by his head on a pole, and have his arms suspended long from the ground; then command the assistant to seize the hip of the thigh, and let another assistant hold the patient as well, who should grab the thigh in shape, for the joints will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is out of place, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has gout, and pulls the ligament above the affected leg properly, and also above the knee; then put the splints, one at the head and one at the foot, then stick the splint between the knees of the patient incorrectly positioned limb; and plant damp cloth around it to prevent the patient from bleeding, then extend each minister towards him, and the mirror places its hand on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns [to its place], that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, put it on a table and press as we have said in the gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it must be straightened quickly, as I have said; and place the hand on the opposite side of the injured angle, then press with the other hand and pull towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is at the shoulder, one should not extend the patient's arm downwards or lift it up, but rather make him lie as if his hip had been dislocated on the opposite side, as we have said in the lying on two hips; and he should be placed on his backside, and the limb extended as we have said before, and press upon the joint at the table. The patient will extend his legs when ready, and they will become even. Then align the thighs, place the pillow underneath, and tie one bandage so that the shoulder does not move; let it rest for 3 or 4 days, then release it, place the pillow again; and if you see that they are equal, tie as before, and let it rest for 3 days. Then release it, and make him walk gently until his limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation in the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: inside and out, backward; and never forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his knee, and if it does not fold up at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you have the patient sit upright, extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his front, and put his foot on your feet; then take his thigh with your hands, pull it apart between your hands, then bend both sides of the thigh inwardly forming a V; another servant extends his foot until the thigh returns to its place, and the sign is that it should be easily bent at the knee again; apply the plaster, and hold the leg to the knee tightly, and bandage them together strongly for three or four days, then release it; do not let the patient walk, until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not straight, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of dislocation, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	about the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 The signs are that the ankle is swollen and protruding at the part where it is dislocated; the repositioning is easy, and it should be extended gently with hands when only swollen.
